Current Affairs Commentary

Canada's New Commercial Treaties with the United States and Japan 13

— Ang

Canada recently signed a reciprocal trade agreement with the United States in Washington and is also said to have reached a commercial agreement with Japan to end the tariff war. This news initially came from Tokyo, and then similar news came from Ottawa. Although both reports were vague and there have been no follow-up reports to date, the result of the Canadian parliamentary election in October of this year was that Mr. King of the Liberal Party replaced Mr. Bennett of the Conservative Party to form a new government. Its economic policy will inevitably undergo changes. The revision of the commercial treaty between Japan and Canada was already a concrete possibility.

Today's economic relations between Japan and Canada are based on the commercial treaty of 1913. At that time, Canada ranked ninth and Japan ranked twelfth in world trade. Before 1932, Canada's trade volume often exceeded Japan's, but by 1933, Canada still ranked ninth, while Japan surpassed it to rank seventh. Japan has consistently been Canada's third or fourth most important market. Up to the end of March of this year, Canadian goods exported to Japan totaled US$17 million, while Japanese goods exported to Canada were only US$8 million. Although the amounts are not large, they are sufficient to prove that Canada still maintains its trade surplus with Japan.

Since the outbreak of the world economic panic, countries have vigorously devalued their currencies and dumped goods, especially Japan. Canada is an agricultural country, but its textile, rubber, and other industries are quite concerned about competition from Japanese goods, so it implemented exchange dumping taxes and tax conversion systems to protect itself. These two types of protective tariffs are not specifically aimed at Japan, but they have the most severe impact on Japanese goods. Japan repeatedly negotiated with the Canadian government to no avail, and on July 20 of this year, it first decided to implement a trade protection law, imposing retaliatory tariffs of 50% ad valorem on eight major products of Canada, including timber, wheat, flour, pulp, woolen cloth, wrapping paper, and bran. Canada was not to be outdone and immediately announced an additional tax of 33 and 1/3% on all Japanese goods. This form of economic struggle against Japan was indeed promoted by the 1932 Ottawa Conference of the British Empire. Is Canada's compromise with Japan now a sign of the disintegration of the Ottawa economic bloc's power?

Canada's economic tendency to move away from Britain seems to be clearly reflected in the commercial treaty signed with the United States on the 15th of last month. The initiation of the US-Canada reciprocal trade agreement dates back to 1911. The reason why negotiations have not been successful over the years is partly due to the difficulty in resolving reciprocal goods and partly due to the opposition of the conservative elements holding power in Canada to independent actions away from Britain. Now, those in power in Canada are the Liberal Party with a strong tendency away from the center. The leader of the party, Mr. King, predicted during the election in October that the US-Canada commercial treaty would be completed within three months. Now it can be said that he has fulfilled his words.

The newly signed US-Canada reciprocal trade agreement will take effect on New Year's Day next year. President Roosevelt called this agreement a "revolution in trade relations between the two countries." On the one hand, this agreement will enable 60 kinds of Canadian goods to open up new markets, and Canada will reduce tariffs on two-thirds of American goods. On the other hand, this agreement is a major blow to the economic nationalism of the British Empire. US Secretary of State Hull once said that the turmoil in the world political situation is due to economic nationalism as its acute stage, and to rebuild the foundation of peace, it is necessary to start with improving international economic relations. Therefore, after the failure of the World Economic Conference in June 1933, the United States has been conducting reciprocal trade policies with various countries separately, successively concluding commercial treaties with Cuba, Brazil, Colombia, Haiti, and other countries. After the establishment of the US-Canada commercial treaty, it also signed a reciprocal trade agreement with Honduras. This policy of the United States clearly deviates from the claim of the former British Foreign Secretary Hoare to redistribute world resources. In the future, the economic contradictions between Britain and the United States will inevitably become more profound, and the US authorities' intention to rebuild the foundation of peace is just empty words.

Naval Conference Adjourns, Reopens January 6 Next Year 14

London – The Naval Conference decided today to adjourn from Saturday until January 6 next year. (National Telegram on the 19th)

London – The Naval Conference is scheduled to continue today. This is the last meeting before the Christmas holiday. The holiday will last until January 6 next year. Representatives from France and Italy will return to their countries for the holidays. Most of the American representatives will use the holidays to travel abroad, with the majority going to Paris. Others have accepted invitations from British friends to spend the holidays here. As for the Japanese representatives, they will all temporarily leave Britain, with most planning to go to Paris, and the rest to the French Riviera to enjoy the warm sunshine, which is better than the gloomy weather in England. (Havas News Agency, 20th)

London – The First Committee resumed at 10:30 am on the 19th. Chairman Monsell proposed extending the Christmas holiday period to January 6, and representatives from all countries expressed their agreement. Then, discussions began on the British draft declaration on shipbuilding. US Representative Davis clarified the US government's position and stated that the US government was considering the issue with a sympathetic attitude. Representatives from France and Italy also expressed their approval of the decision, but pointed out that its application still needs to be studied. Finally, the Japanese plenipotentiaries Nagano and Nagai took turns speaking, raising important questions about the British proposal. According to the preamble of the draft declaration on shipbuilding, each government needs to autonomously declare the necessary military equipment for its national security. However, how to determine the minimum limit of naval power for each country? Japan will never theoretically or practically acknowledge the existing strength based on the provisions of the Washington and London treaties. The Japanese government is dissatisfied with the existing naval power based on the ratio system and abandoned the Washington Treaty, so determining the required quantity based on the existing strength cannot guarantee national defense security. British representatives Monsell and Chatfield refuted these questions. The meeting adjourned at 1 pm. (Japan United Press, 19th)

The Paris Plan Fails, the League of Nations Council Resolves: Expresses Gratitude for the Peace Efforts of Britain and France, Entrusts the Thirteen Committee to Re-examine the Overall Situation, and Continues to Monitor Sanctions Against Italy 15

Geneva – The Council of the League of Nations continued to discuss the peace plan of Britain and France yesterday afternoon at 5:30, and concluded at 6:10 after a short period. First, the Soviet representative, Ambassador to France Potemkin, spoke, strongly opposing the peace plan of Britain and France, saying that it contradicted the principles of the League's Covenant, and proposed a draft resolution, advocating that the Council firmly reject the British and French plan. Then, Turkish representative Rushdi stood up and said that the Council should not condemn the efforts of Britain and France to mediate the dispute, and immediately proposed a draft resolution containing three points:

Express gratitude to Britain and France for proposing a peace plan.

This plan is only preliminary in nature and cannot be used by the Council to take any decision.

Entrust the Thirteen-Nation Small Group Committee to re-examine the entire case of the Italian-Abyssinian dispute based on the principles of the League's Covenant.

This draft resolution was unanimously adopted by all directors. British Minister Without Portfolio Eden then said that although the peace plan has failed, the situation of the sanctions issue has not changed as a result. After the Council adjourned, the Eighteen-Nation Small Group Committee met immediately afterwards, for a very short time, with only the chairman, Portuguese representative Vasco Valerio, announcing that the committee of experts on monitoring the implementation of sanctions is continuing its work. (Havas News Agency, 20th)

Geneva – Before the Council of the League of Nations passed the resolution, it had a long secret consultation on the second article, and then decided to delete the phrase "when the two parties have not replied," because it felt that the Council could not continue to handle this suggestion. (Reuters, 19th)

Geneva – The Thirteen-Nation Small Group Committee of the League of Nations Council is scheduled to meet on January 10 or 12 next year. There is little hope of re-considering the peace plan proposed by Britain and France. This plan will almost become a page in history. According to observers here, the task of the Thirteen-Nation Small Group Committee in accordance with the resolution passed by the Council yesterday is to "find appropriate ways to stop the Italian-Abyssinian war." Therefore, the basis for negotiations on the Italian-Abyssinian dispute will be found by the committee itself. (Havas News Agency, 20th)

Geneva – The Council of the League of Nations is rumored to meet in mid-January next year. The Eighteen-Nation Small Group Committee must be convened as late as around January 20. (Havas News Agency, 20th)

Eden and Laval Leave Geneva for Home 16

Paris – Premier and Foreign Minister Laval and British Minister Without Portfolio Eden are currently jointly traveling from here to Geneva to attend the meeting of the League of Nations Council. Now that the matter is over, they arrived here from Geneva together at 8:15 this morning. (Havas News Agency, 20th)

Abyssinian Government Sends Letter to Britain and France, Rejects Peace Proposal, Determined to Maintain Territorial Integrity, Hopes the League Will Stop Aggression 17

Addis Ababa – The Abyssinian government recently submitted a memorandum to the British and French ministers, expressing its rejection of the solution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute proposed by those countries. Once this plan is implemented, "Abyssinia will establish a political system that is even worse than the trusteeship system, the principles contained in the League's Covenant will be abandoned, and the situation of Abyssinia being divided will be formed." The Abyssinian government is determined to maintain territorial integrity to the last moment, hoping that the League will take necessary measures to stop the war of aggression. (Havas News Agency, 19th)

Italy Has Not Yet Replied 18

Rome – According to official sources today, the Italian government has not yet drafted a reply to the Paris peace plan. Although British Prime Minister Baldwin has said that the plan has been abandoned, the Italian government seems to be following the Abyssinian government's approach of replying to the League, neither accepting nor rejecting it, and letting the League reject it. (Reuters, 20th)

British Parliament Heatedly Debates Diplomacy, Baldwin's Cabinet Wins Victory, Labour Party's Impeachment Motion Ultimately Rejected, Hoare Takes the Blame and is Sacrificed 19

London – The House of Commons discussed the government's diplomatic policy and the solution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute proposed by Britain and France this afternoon. Prime Minister Baldwin delivered an important speech, and the House voted 390 to 165 to express confidence in the government. The position of the cabinet has been temporarily stabilized, at least in the parliamentary aspect. However, the House was rather cold to Baldwin's declaration. A large part of the cabinet's victory was due to the opposition Labour Party's ineffective attack. When the party leader, Major Attlee, began to speak, Conservative Party members who were dissatisfied with the British-French plan withdrew from the meeting, thus stabilizing the cabinet's position. Major Attlee's attack on the British-French plan involved Baldwin's personal reputation, which was not approved by the House of Commons. This was also a reason for the cabinet's victory. Former Foreign Secretary Austen Chamberlain refuted it, saying that Prime Minister Baldwin's personal reputation was not damaged in the slightest, and most members should support him. He also said that Britain should still assist the League of Nations, but only within the scope of collective action, without any ambiguity that would allow Britain's true intentions to be misunderstood. The plan proposed by Britain and France has aroused suspicion, but its original intention was not to disappoint the League of Nations. (Havas News Agency, 19th)

London – The British government has won a victory in today's extremely important debate in the House of Commons on the British-French peace plan. After Prime Minister Baldwin disclosed British foreign policy and explained his advocacy of collective security, the House rejected the Labour Party's impeachment motion by a vote of 397 to 165, and passed Winterton's amendment by a vote of 390 to 165.

Original Text of the Labour Party's Impeachment Motion 20

The original text of the impeachment motion is roughly as follows: "The conditions proposed by the government as the basis for resolving the Italian-Abyssinian war are actually a reward for the aggressor, destroy collective security, and violate the wishes expressed by the people and the spirit of the League of Nations. Therefore, the House of Commons demands the immediate cancellation of these conditions." Winterton's amendment, on the one hand, stated that any conditions for resolving the Italian-Abyssinian dispute must be acceptable to the League of Nations, and on the other hand, expressed its willingness to fully support the government in promoting the foreign policy stated in the government's statement, which was supported by the people during the recent general election.

During the debate, the meeting was extremely crowded, with the public gallery filled with diplomats from various countries and important figures, and the Prince was also among them.

Attlee Challenges the Government 21

After former Foreign Secretary Hoare explained the reasons for his resignation, Labour Party leader Attlee proposed an impeachment motion, saying that he expressed great sympathy for Sir Hoare, because the entire government was responsible for Hoare's actions. Hoare only took the blame for others. Since Hoare should resign, the government should also resign. This peace plan cedes half of Abyssinia in exchange for a corridor for camels, sacrifices the aggressed, and grants the greatest concessions to the aggressor. This is not British justice. Collective security and the League of Nations itself will be destroyed by it. The people recognize this clause as a breach of faith by the government in the election, because the electors did not support the government for this reason. Even if there is an immediate danger of war, the government has no reason to take this action. The government should declare that the League of Nations has failed, revoke the sanctions, and should not encourage the aggressor with more concessions than the aggressor wants. This is simply an act of betraying the Abyssinian people. When Hoare urgently needed rest, the cabinet entrusted him with the most difficult task. Before Hoare went to Paris, what instructions did the cabinet give him? This is what the country wants to know.

Baldwin Defends with All His Might 22

Prime Minister Baldwin spoke with great excitement, first praising Hoare, saying that Hoare still believed that his actions did not go beyond the scope of the League of Nations. His actions were not satisfactory, so he resigned to apologize. At this time, Hoare's resignation was not only a great loss to the government, but also a loss felt by the people, because he was loved by the people. The day Hoare went to Paris happened to be a Sunday. There was no contact, and it was not until the next day that he learned that the agreement had been reached. On Monday morning, he received a letter from Hoare asking the cabinet members to support what he had done. When the government had not had time to study it, this matter had been leaked out. Should the cabinet support or deny the actions of a cabinet member? This is what the cabinet needs to discuss. The cabinet members were not satisfied with this plan, and thought that the measures were inappropriate, but the main responsibility should be borne by him (the Prime Minister himself), so he immediately decided that he must maintain his colleague who was abroad. He did not think it strange that the opposition expressed their feelings, but he did not expect that so many Conservative Party members across the country would have such deep feelings based on conscience and honor. He knew that he was not supported by the majority of public opinion, but if the government ultimately submitted this plan to the League of Nations, judging from the current situation, this plan has completely died. The British government does not want to find a way to revive it. The British government has always remained unchanged in its position, that is, British policy is based on the League of Nations. He is willing to always abide by the policy of collective security. If Britain had to participate in a unilateral war, he was afraid that there would be a backlash in the country. People often said that if Britain supported the League of Nations and was in a position to independently exercise what all countries should do together, then we would no longer allow the government to abide by this collective security, because the decision to wage war would not only be in the Mediterranean, but perhaps closer to Britain. The Prime Minister continued to speak about the effectiveness of sanctions, saying that if the world and the League of Nations acted immediately in unison, the sanctions could be completely effective, but today we have not yet reached this point. Therefore, if the League of Nations, when imposing sanctions, reaches the point where the aggressor is not subject to these sanctions and will resist the League of Nations, then the League of Nations will surely obtain the guarantee that all those with power must support it and will immediately support it. The last sanction of the League of Nations is indeed a great force, but if it cannot be implemented immediately, it will be useless. Because it cannot be implemented immediately, there is a danger of gradually dragging various countries into the war without knowing where it will end. If the free countries of Europe today want to maintain their security, they must carefully consider that the assistance that small countries hoping for the League of Nations can obtain is that the powerful countries in the League of Nations are prepared to come out to assist them in case of emergency. We have now moved from the stage of empty words to the stage of action. The Prime Minister finally asked the House to give him trust. After the speech, there was great applause.

Chamberlain Rises to Support 23

Former Foreign Secretary Austen Chamberlain then rose to speak in defense of the Prime Minister. The gist of his words was that it was a matter of public affairs, not our own affairs. This is the true meaning of the League of Nations. If other countries all did what Britain did, then the League of Nations could escape from its difficult situation, and it would be more difficult for aggressors to do what they want in the future.

Winterton Proposes Amendment 24

When Winterton proposed the amendment, he said that advocating military sanctions or similar military sanctions that could have the effect of causing Italy to resist by force is an act with criminal responsibility. If the oil embargo is implemented, causing Italy's armed resistance, then this action would conflict with the government's promise in the general election.

Labour Party Members Question Again 25

Labour Party member Dalton asked Finance Minister Chamberlain whether he could announce the selection of the new Foreign Secretary. Chamberlain shook his head and did not answer. Dalton also asked whether the government intended to continue the oil embargo, and said that the Prime Minister's words were very unclear. The Labour Party must propose an impeachment. Chamberlain replied that this tragedy had caused the government to lose the service of Sir Hoare. The only comfort the government had was that Sir Hoare had the opportunity to recover his health because of this. He hoped that Sir Hoare would be able to resume political affairs soon. The government had taken responsibility for what the country now considered a mistake.

Admits to Obtaining French Guarantee 26

Someone asked whether the government had inquired about the attitude of the major powers if Britain were attacked by Italy. The Finance Minister replied that if war broke out, the location must be in the Mediterranean, so what should be known is the attitude of the Mediterranean countries, not the attitude of other member states far from the Mediterranean. The British government has inquired about the attitude of other countries, but the attitude of France is very important. The rumor that Britain has not obtained guarantees from several countries is incorrect. If the League of Nations decides to implement the oil embargo, if the British government is well aware that the relevant member states of the League of Nations are all prepared to participate to deal with sudden attacks, then Britain will of course be prepared to do its part and support the implementation of the oil embargo.

No Change in Foreign Policy 27

In short, the British government's attitude towards the League of Nations has not changed in the slightest. We must take advantage of all opportunities to negotiate an acceptable peace, but if we cannot, we still advocate collective action to seek collective security. However, it must be known that the League of Nations' final sanction must come from force. If the member states of the League of Nations are not prepared to use force to deal with the threat of the aggressor, then it cannot be hoped to be completely successful. (Reuters, 19th)

A Battle of Wits in the House of Lords 28

London – The House of Lords and the House of Commons met simultaneously today to debate diplomatic matters. Many noble ladies gathered in the special public gallery. First, former Liberal Party member of the House of Commons, Lord Davies, began by asking the House of Lords to declare that it could not accept the peace plan and did not approve of any solution that did not conform to the principles of fairness and Britain's obligations to the League of Nations. Davies also urged the government to continue the policy announced by Hoare in Geneva in September, and said that Europe, the United States, and the British Dominions were greatly shocked by this peace plan. The plan has indelibly stained Britain's glory and reputation, and the government has curbed the rising tide of cooperation between the United States and the League of Nations. Lord Privy Seal Halifax replied on behalf of the government, saying that it was not the task of the League of Nations to start a war in Europe to stop the war in Africa. The danger of the war expanding is unimaginable. When Hoare took the road to Paris to Switzerland, he did not order to discuss peace or reconciliation conditions with French Premier Laval. Hoare was involuntarily drawn into the discussion. These conditions were first published in detail in French newspapers. When the British government received them, because the newspapers had already disclosed them, it felt that it had to make a decision. The government did not approve of these conditions when it read them. He need not hide this. The government did not initially expect the public to react to this clause. This is indeed something that cannot be shirked. He thought that Hoare's resignation was enough to thank the people. The spiritual leadership position that Britain has gained in recent months can be consolidated again in the world. The Archbishop of Canterbury then spoke, expressing concern about the government's handling of this most unfortunate Paris peace plan. He said that he hoped that the sanctions policy would continue and that the British government should refuse to participate in any solution that seemed to respect the aggressor's behavior. Lord Allen of Hurtwood delivered a thorough speech, saying that he did not believe Mussolini was making empty threats. He had never taken this action. Mussolini would rather fight with France or fight with us or fight with Britain alone than give in. We cannot now return to the policy of security first announced in September. Unless we are prepared to support any sanctions that can force Mussolini to stop the war, we cannot relieve our position in the League of Nations or the country. Lord Allen's conclusion said, "I have to make a decision, that is, in the danger of the Mediterranean war, the serious development in Europe or the Far East, the only right way is to advance without retreat." Then, Lord Ponsonby expressed doubts about Hoare being suddenly forced to discuss peace in Paris. Lord Strabolgi then expressed sympathy for Ponsonby's doubts and asked, "If it is credible, then what was discussed before Paris?" Finally, Lord Stanhope concluded the debate, saying that British and French experts had indeed discussed the peace conditions in Paris for two weeks, but there seemed to be no possibility of compromise. After Hoare and the experts returned to London, the British cabinet seemed to have ample time to discuss everything, but since it had been leaked by the French newspapers, the British government had to make a decision. Then, Lord Davies' motion was put to a vote and was unanimously passed by the entire House. (Reuters, 19th)

Candidates for Foreign Secretary Successor, Chamberlain's Call is High 29

London – King George V recently summoned Prime Minister Baldwin in the morning, and the cabinet is scheduled to meet in the afternoon. The general public attaches great importance to these two events, because the selection of the Foreign Secretary will be decided by this. It is rumored that Lord Privy Seal Halifax will be transferred to the position of Foreign Secretary. This statement is difficult to realize, but the saying that Finance Minister Neville Chamberlain will be transferred to the position is rampant. According to observers, the most promising candidates are actually Finance Minister Neville Chamberlain and former Foreign Secretary Austen Chamberlain. It is also said that if Austen Chamberlain succeeds as Foreign Secretary, the future relationship between Britain and Italy will inevitably become tense. The transfer of the Finance Minister means that the British government is willing to see the tense relationship between Britain and Italy ease. (Havas News Agency, 20th)

Reactions in Rome; Anglo-Italian Relations to Further Intensify 30

London – Political circles here are wondering what Italian Prime Minister Mussolini's reaction will be to the resignation of Foreign Secretary Hoare. The general belief is that Anglo-Italian relations will become increasingly tense in the coming days. Regarding the sanctions issue, political figures believe that the British government can only implement stricter sanctions if other member states of the League of Nations immediately pledge military assistance (land, sea, and air) to Britain. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

Rome – The semi-official Roman newspaper, "Il Popolo di Roma," recently commented on Prime Minister Mussolini's speech delivered at the new village of Pontinia the day before, saying, "If anyone attempts to seize even an inch of land that we have conquered by military force, we are prepared to resist with all our might. The world should understand this clearly. Neither unfair economic blockades, nor diplomatic trickery, nor violence can shake our resolve. We will not allow those Ethiopians who have already surrendered to return to their government, lest they suffer retaliation." The newspaper concluded, "If other countries force Italy to relinquish its acquired rights and disregard

Page 6

its name, then European peace is truly in danger." (Havas dispatch, 20th)

London Newspapers' Commentary 31

Showing Sympathy for Hoare

London – This morning's newspapers, though politically diverse, all stated that the outstanding figure during yesterday's House of Commons debate on the Anglo-French peace plan was Sir Samuel Hoare, who resigned yesterday as a scapegoat. Prime Minister Baldwin, on the other hand, appeared ashamed. The Morning Post stated that since the government had approved Hoare's policy, it should have supported Hoare through thick and thin, which would have been the honorable thing to do. The Daily Telegraph reported that Baldwin seemed completely unprepared for the intensity of the storm caused by the peace plan. The News Chronicle stated that it was not Baldwin who saved the government, but rather the leader of the opposition party, Attlee, whose speech far exceeded the standards expected in this debate, and whose accusations against Baldwin's honor were also a strategic error. The Times stated that Hoare's resignation was a temporary pause in his political career, not its end. The government clearly acknowledged the legitimacy of public opinion and rescinded its hasty decision, thus quelling the wave of opposition. (Reuters dispatch, 20th)

French Premier Laval Denies Thoughts of Resigning 32

Determined to Carry Out Policies to the End

Geneva – French Prime Minister Laval informed the press tonight that the rumors of his intention to resign are untrue. He has no such thought and is prepared to persevere in the Chamber of Deputies to carry out his policies to the end. (Reuters dispatch, 17th)

Paris – Rumors are circulating that the position of the Laval cabinet has become unfavorable and is in danger of collapsing after Minister Without Portfolio Herriot resigned as leader of the Radical Socialist Party. After inquiring with members of parliament, this newspaper has learned that this is incorrect. The Chamber of Deputies is scheduled to discuss questions on the 27th (questions on foreign policy), to which Prime Minister Laval will personally respond. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

Reasons for Herriot's Resignation as Party Leader 33

Paris – Minister Without Portfolio Herriot recently sent a letter to the Executive Committee of the Radical Socialist Party, explaining his reasons for resigning as party leader, saying, "I have long felt the contradictions between my humble position as party leader and my participation in the cabinet as a representative of the party." He stated that as a cabinet member, he should have the freedom to act, but this is incompatible with the party's demands. The personal pain he has endured is beyond description. Herriot's political friends tried to persuade him to withdraw his resignation letter, but to no avail. A new party leader for the Radical Socialist Party may not be elected for some time. Party members believe that former Prime Minister Jeanneney, a senator, is the most likely candidate. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

French Budget Approved by the Chamber of Deputies 34

Paris – The Chamber of Deputies recently passed the entire 1936 budget with a vote of 272 to 166. The expenditure portion totals 40,431,074,000 francs, and the revenue portion totals 4,534,051,000 francs, leaving a surplus of 102,978,000 francs. The Senate is scheduled to begin discussing the budget tomorrow. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

Fierce Battle Between Italian and Ethiopian Armies on the Northern Front 35

Ethiopian Army Strategically Launches a Two-Pronged Counterattack; Repelled by Machine Guns South of Magale

Asmara – Italian military authorities announced today that the Ethiopian army, which launched a counterattack south of Magale, has been repelled by Italian machine guns. However, there was previously a fierce battle. (National Telegraph, 19th)

Addis Ababa – Our special correspondent, O'Chenay, reports that news regarding the fighting on the Tigre front on the northern front is both vague and contradictory from both the Italian and Ethiopian sides. What is known is that the positions of the two armies on the front line have not changed much recently. The Ethiopian army's plan was originally to divide its forces into two groups to attack the flanks of the Italian army on the northern front. The right flank army, personally commanded by General Seyoum, the governor of Tigre Province, made progress and came into contact with the Italian army near the Taigas River two days ago. As for the left flank army, commanded by General Kassa Sebhat, it advanced northwest towards the city of Magale. Due to the vague nature of previous war reports, it is still difficult to judge the value of this operation. (Havas dispatch, 20th)

Dessie – Preparations for Emperor Haile Selassie to inspect the northern front lines are almost complete. His cavalry is adorned with dazzling gold embroidery. The Emperor is bringing twenty Arabian thoroughbreds, all trained for mountain climbing, as well as two gold saddles. His retinue and guards consist of one hundred and twenty horses and one hundred and fifty mules, all draped in red cloth. There are five tents, lined with red, green, and blue silk, for dining, sleeping, and writing. Another large tent is used for prayer, and its protection is the responsibility of the squadron leader. Emperor Haile Selassie is wearing yellow military garb, and the Crown Prince is also accompanying him. (Reuters dispatch, 20th)

Chairman of the US Senate Foreign Relations Committee, Pittman, Delivers Speech on the US-Japan Crisis 36

Japan's Ambitions Resemble Those of Germany's Wilhelm; US and Japan Inevitably Headed for War in the Pacific

Las Vegas, USA – Senator Pittman, Chairman of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee, stated today in a speech at the local Rotary Club that the Japanese government's ambitions are quite similar to those of former German Emperor Wilhelm, and that its ultimate goal is to conquer the world. If this continues, the United States, for the sake of self-defense in the Pacific, will have no choice but to go to war. Japan's conquest of China is the preliminary plan for its imperialism. "Sooner or later, the United States must also fight for its survival. If we delay too long, the outcome will be difficult to predict." Pittman described the United States' Far East policy, saying, "We can either retreat and lie dormant, or we can decide on our final stance and no longer retreat." Pittman further stated that Japan will seize the Philippines as soon as it has the opportunity. Pittman then turned to commenting on the world situation, saying, "The failure of the League of Nations is undeniable, especially in dealing with Japan. Japan seizes every opportunity when various countries in the world are facing difficulties to expand its territory. Japan is now taking advantage of Britain's entanglement in Europe and the United States' pacifism, causing these countries to be caught off guard. I deeply resent the policy of appeasement towards Japan. At the London conference, the Japanese representative again stated that, fearing a war in the Pacific, insisting on naval equality is truly unbearable. Japan fears only two things: the navies of Britain and the United States. If the navies of the two countries simultaneously conducted exercises near Japan in the Pacific, Japan could be subdued without a single soldier or bullet." Pittman emphasized the importance of the Nine-Power Treaty, saying that Japan has blatantly violated it, demonstrating its contempt for other governments. "I am not trying to create alarm, but the American people should have someone tell them where the danger lies. Once Japan dominates China, it will become an unrivaled world power and can proceed to realize its dream of conquering the world. Although I support neutrality, in such circumstances, we must formulate a policy early and stick to it to the end." (National Telegraph, 19th)

US Air Force Expansion Plan 37

2,400 Aircraft to be Built in Three Years; Army Chief of Staff Submits Plan to House Appropriations Committee

Washington – US Army Chief of Staff Craig today submitted to the House Appropriations Committee a three-year plan to build 800 military aircraft each year, at an annual cost of $70 million. Military Affairs Committee Chairman McSwain stated today that although the government hopes to balance the budget, he supports this plan. (National Telegraph, 20th)

New Japanese Aircraft Carrier Completed 38

Tokyo – The aircraft carrier "Soryu" (10,000 tons), which was built at the Kure Naval Dockyard, is scheduled to be launched at 9:00 AM on the 23rd. The ship is one of two new aircraft carriers permitted under the Washington Treaty. Its displacement is 15,000 tons, its speed is 30 knots, and it is equipped with twelve 12.7 cm guns, which are cutting-edge weapons. Construction began in November of Showa 9 (1934). (Nichi-Ren Telegraph, 20th)

Approaching Opening of the 68th Japanese Diet 39

Tokyo – The 68th Diet is scheduled to open on the 24th. It will be adjourned from the 28th to January 20th of next year and will resume on the 21st. After Prime Minister Okada and Foreign Minister Hirota deliver policy speeches on domestic and foreign policy in the House of Peers and the House of Representatives, political battles will begin. Opposition to the government from the Seiyukai party is strong in this Diet, and there is talk of submitting a motion of no confidence in the government. It is also possible that the government will dissolve the Diet. (Nichi-Ren Telegraph, 20th)

Cotton Cloth and Rayon Imported from China 40

Egypt Levying Additional Taxes to Counter Japanese Goods

Cairo – Today, the Egyptian government ordered that a foreign exchange compensation surtax of 43% be levied on cotton and rayon goods imported from China. According to customs reports, since the implementation of this tax on Japanese goods, a large number of goods have been shipped from China to Egypt, but in reality, they are all Japanese goods. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

Cairo – The government issued an order yesterday to levy an additional import tax of 40% on cotton textiles and rayon imported from China. According to the treaty between Egypt and Japan, since the government announced its abolition, it has levied an additional import tax of 40% on Japanese goods since September 20th of this year. Subsequently, customs officers reported that a large number of cotton textiles and rayon imported from China are suspected of being produced in Japan and re-exported from China in the hope of avoiding paying the above-mentioned additional tax. After investigation by the government, it was decided to issue the above-mentioned order to restrict tax evasion. (Havas dispatch, 20th)

London Silver Market Eases 41

US Purchases 4 Million Ounces in Bombay

London – The London silver market eased somewhat today as the United States took in 4 million ounces in the Bombay market, a quarter of which had previously been intended for sale in London. This eased tensions here. Today's sales in London amounted to approximately 16.5 million ounces, with the United States purchasing 6% of it. Buyers are now trying to buy one-month futures at a price of 20 pence, and sellers are gradually limiting sales prices, which shows an improvement in the psychology of speculators. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

London – London brokers have decided to close the silver market every Saturday and Sunday. (Reuters dispatch, 20th)

Washington – US Treasury Secretary Morgenthau reiterated today that the US Treasury Department is still buying silver but did not say where it is buying it. Morgenthau claimed that he had bought silver every day this week, and the purchase locations were quite numerous and unexpected. Morgenthau declined to say whether the purchases were from private individuals or from the government. Morgenthau also said that although there are no buyers in London, New York can still determine the price of silver, which is very noteworthy. Since London has no market, New York has no other choice. Morgenthau also stated that the US government has purchased 72 million ounces of newly mined silver produced in Mexico in the past year at New York prices. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

Oklahoma – Senator Elmer Thomas suggested today that Congress seek opinions on silver monetization immediately after its opening in January of next year. Thomas also telegraphed Treasury Secretary Morgenthau, requesting his best efforts to assist and guarantee the implementation of the silver purchase plan with various financial resources, and stated that if domestic and foreign forces opposing the silver purchase policy could eliminate the program, the silver already purchased by the Treasury Department would suffer great losses. Reactionaries at home and abroad are attacking the government's silver policy, causing the price of silver to fall, which is a monetary war manipulating international exchange rates, international currency, and world trade. (National Telegraph, 19th)

Japanese Soldiers Invade Mongolian Territory 42

Opening Fire with Machine Guns, Causing Numerous Mongolian Casualties

Moscow – A dispatch from Kulun reports that on the 18th, more than 20 Japanese soldiers in vehicles appeared near the position of the Mongolian border guards at Bulundetson, southwest of Lake Baynor. The Mongolian guards immediately signaled that they had entered Mongolian territory, and they returned to Manchurian territory. However, at 9:00 AM on the 19th, ten more vehicles arrived at Bulundetson, including a passenger car and an ambulance. The passenger car contained two Japanese officers and one White Russian, and each vehicle carried 25 armed soldiers. They also carried five machine guns. Without warning, they surrounded the Mongolian guard post and opened fire on the Mongolian soldiers with machine guns. The commander of the post, under orders to avoid conflict with the Japanese and Manchurian sides, ordered the border guards to retreat, but the Japanese continued to fire. As a result, many Mongolians were killed, the number of which is unknown. According to reliable reports, the deputy director of the post and six Mongolian soldiers were indeed killed. A detailed investigation is currently underway. Kulun was outraged upon hearing this news. (TASS dispatch, 19th)

Changsha – The Kwantung Army Headquarters announced that on the morning of the 19th, Colonel Oyama, the commander of the border surveillance team of "Manchukuo," intended to establish a surveillance post near Ulatga and Baolundis, west of Burgol. While advancing, he clashed with 70 Outer Mongolian soldiers holding machine guns who had illegally crossed the border and invaded the vicinity of Ulahotga. Colonel Oyama and others immediately expelled them. At that time, ten soldiers, including cavalry Captain Nagata, who were investigating the vicinity, also participated in the battle due to their duties. The enemy abandoned 20 rifles and retreated southward. The Japanese army suffered no casualties. (Dentsu Telegraph, 6th)

New Railroads to be Built in Manchuria 43

Feng Yuxiang Issues Written Statement 44

Coming for the Sake of National Crisis; Only Unity Can Save the Nation; I Dare Not Decline Any Difficult or Arduous Work

Nanjing – This reporter visited Feng Yuxiang on the afternoon of the 20th and inquired about the date of his appointment as Deputy Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission. He issued the following written statement: "The position is too high, and the responsibility is too heavy, so I dare not take it. Moreover, Yuxiang comes from the ranks and is uneducated and unskilled, as the comrades in the Central Committee know. I have decided to come for the sake of the national crisis, knowing only that without unity, the nation cannot be saved. I am content that the comrades in the Central Committee do not abandon me and allow me to participate in the country's major plans. I dare not have any hope beyond that. As for any difficult or arduous work, I dare not decline. These words come from the bottom of my heart. Please forgive me, comrades." (Central News Agency dispatch, 20th)

Legislative Yuan Approves Budgets for Five Provinces and Municipalities 48

Vice President Ye Chucang Attends and Delivers Remarks

Nanjing – The Legislative Yuan held its 40th meeting on the morning of the 20th, with 68 members including Luo Yunyan in attendance. President Sun Ke and Vice President Ye also attended, with Secretary-General Liang Hancao present. Items discussed: the general budget of local ordinary revenue and expenditure for the 24th year of the Republic for Nanjing Municipality; the general budget of local ordinary revenue and expenditure for the 23rd year of the Republic for the three provinces of Jiangsu, Gansu, and Ningxia; the supplementary general budget of local ordinary revenue and expenditure for the 23rd year of the Republic for Qingdao Municipality. Resolutions: All were approved as proposed, based on the results of the review by the Finance Committee. (Central News Agency dispatch, 20th)

Nanjing – At the conclusion of the regular meeting of the Legislative Yuan on the morning of the 20th, President Sun stood up to introduce Vice President Ye, as it was Ye's first time attending a meeting of the Yuan, and then invited Ye to speak. Ye modestly addressed the legislators as "teachers" and explained, "The Legislative Yuan is a place where specialized talents gather. I have neither learning nor strengths. Aside from attending classes and reading books, there is nothing I can say here. Over the years, I have served in party departments and various political circles, and the knowledge I have gained, as incomplete as it may be, I am confident has not come solely from books. The knowledge and experience I have gained at meetings are indeed not small. Since the 16th year of the Republic [1927], my life for the past eight years has almost entirely been spent in meeting rooms. At every meeting, I have listened attentively and benefited greatly. However, the materials I have obtained from attending various meetings in the past still seem simple and cannot compare to the richness of the Legislative Yuan. Being able to attend here is no different from the President giving me the opportunity to attend classes and read books. From now on, I will be able to hear everyone's high opinions often. I would like to express my special thanks to all of you teachers." After his speech, the entire room responded with enthusiastic applause. Historically, Vice Presidents attending meetings of the Legislative Yuan are rare. Aside from Lin Sen, who attended one meeting when Hu Hanmin was President of the Yuan, Ye is perhaps only the second person to do so. Therefore, all the legislators felt a doubled sense of interest in Ye's attendance. At noon, Sun hosted a banquet for Ye at the Yuan's Mingzhi Building, inviting dozens of people to accompany him, including the chairmen and conveners of various committees, such as Chuan Bingchang, Wu Jingxiong, Ma Yinchu, Wu Shangying, He Sui, Huang Youchang, Liu Kejun, and Liang Hancao. They dispersed only after enjoying themselves thoroughly. (Central News Agency dispatch, 20th)

Central Bank Reorganized as Preparatory Bank 52

Ordinary Banking Business to be Merged Separately; May be Achieved by New Year's Day if Time Permits

Nanjing – Since preparations began for the reorganization of the Central Bank into the Central Reserve Bank, the organizational law has been revised. A portion of the ordinary banking business currently operated by the Central Bank will be handled by the Bank of China, and another portion, such as trust and mortgage services, will be taken over by the Central Trust Bureau. The reorganization date may be achieved by New Year's Day of the 25th year of the Republic [1936] if time permits. Of the commercial shares received, 49% are currently being contacted by other banks to purchase shares. In the future, the majority of commercial shares will be purchased by the banking sector. As for the Real Estate Mortgage Bank, it has been decided to allocate a large sum of money to establish it separately. Its name is tentatively set as the Industrial Bank to simplify matters. As for the plan to establish provincial and county banks widely, the previously proposed methods have reportedly not been determined and are being studied separately. The date of implementation still seems to be pending. (Special dispatch, 20th)

Xu Shiying Submits Resignation Again 60

Nanjing: Xu Shiying went to the Executive Yuan on the morning of the 20th to meet with President Jiang, and was received by Weng Wenhao. At a time when people's livelihoods are declining and the economy is scarce, it will be increasingly difficult to raise funds for disaster relief in the future. He personally felt old and weak, and mentally and physically exhausted, and was willing to retire immediately. The Executive Yuan has issued instructions in the afternoon to retain him. Panama's Harsh Regulations: Overseas Chinese Businessmen Win Appeal 75

Nanjing: According to information from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Panamanian Congress passed commercial regulations in September of last year, restricting foreign nationals by stipulating that the number of stores established by nationals of the same country must be proportional to the number of their residents in Panama, with one store allowed for every 100 people, called a "quota store." All extra stores must pay a business tax of 75 to 200 yuan. The implementation of these regulations has a huge impact on the livelihoods of our overseas Chinese. Our embassy in Panama has repeatedly made serious representations to the Panamanian government, requesting its prompt cancellation, and urging overseas Chinese businessmen in the interior of Panama to appeal according to law. The Panama Supreme Court has now made a final judgment on the 18th of this month that the regulations violate the constitution. Overseas Chinese residents in Panama were extremely happy upon hearing the news. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 20th)

Bail Received by Courts Should be Transferred to the Central Trust Bureau 76

The Ministry of Justice issued another instruction to the high courts of all provinces on the 20th, stipulating that the bail received by the courts from the parties concerned in the future should be deposited in the Central Trust Bureau. All deposit and withdrawal procedures are the same as those of the Central Bank, and interest on current and fixed deposits shall be handled in accordance with regulations. If there is a court but no branch or designated agent of the bureau in the provinces and counties, and if transfer is required, it should be entrusted to the branch or office of the Central Bank for handling. If there is no such bank or office, it should be entrusted to the national tax collection agency for handling. (Special dispatch on the 20th)

Tianjin: Students March and Petition 100

More than a thousand students participated, and all orders were well maintained

Tianjin Correspondence: Since the past half month, middle school students and above in Tianjin have witnessed the difficulties in North China and the patriotic movement of students in various schools in Peiping, and their blood has been boiling. Last week, with the French Business School as the center, the Tianjin Municipal Students' Union of Middle Schools and Above was organized, and a circular was issued to respond to the student movement in Peiping and Tianjin. At that time, it was intended to make further representations, but due to the vigorous persuasion of the principals of various colleges, it was suspended. On the 16th, the students of Peiping and Tianjin had a second movement, and most of the male and female students were arrested, which gave the students in Tianjin a great shock. On the evening of the 17th, students from various schools held a secret meeting at the French Business School and decided to march and demonstrate and petition the municipal government. That evening, the principals of various colleges heard the news and knew that it was difficult to stop them. They gathered at the Women's Normal College and invited Sun Runyu, secretary-general of the municipal government, Liu Yushu, director of the Public Security Bureau, and Li Jinzao, director of the Education Bureau, to discuss ways to eliminate the situation, and hoped that the authorities would explain the truth about the patriotic movement of students in Peiping to the students. The principals of various colleges who were present were Li Shutian, president of Beiyang Institute of Technology; Huang Zijian, secretary-general of Nankai University; Yang Yizhou, president of the French Business School; Qi Biting, president of the Women's Normal College; Wei Daoming, president of the Industrial College; Zhang Songguan, president of the Fisheries College; Yang Shaoun, president of the Tianjin Normal School; He Kongbin, president of the Tianjin Middle School; Liu Fang, president of Huiwen; etc. The presidents of the colleges stated that Peiping and Tianjin are close to each other, and the student patriotic movement is a legitimate act. The principals of the colleges can only persuade and stop them, but cannot interfere by force. Therefore, it is hoped that the authorities have a good way to deal with it to avoid any movement that will put the two cities of Peiping and Tianjin in unrest. Moreover, young people's thoughts are easily radical. If the authorities guide them according to the situation, it will be easy to quell them. In addition to trying their best to persuade the students of various colleges to study with peace of mind, on the other hand, they earnestly request the authorities in Peiping to not go too far, and should be lenient to the students and release the arrested. Then the students in Tianjin will be less stimulated, or the storm may be quelled invisibly, etc. Sun Runyu and Liu Yushu expressed their opinions separately, hoping that the presidents of the colleges would be responsible for persuading the students to study with peace of mind. The intention of the Tianjin college presidents was to convey it to the Peiping authorities. At 6 pm that night, two telegrams were sent out, one to President Jiang and Minister Wang, and one to the Peiping authorities, requesting the speedy release of the arrested students from various schools. At 8 am on the 18th, more than a thousand male and female students from nine colleges, including Industry, Beiyang, French Business, Fisheries, Jiuzhen, Vocational Business, Tianjin Normal, Women's Normal College, and Industry and Commerce, gathered in the Tianjin Municipal Public Gymnasium in Caijia Garden, Hebei. Representatives from various schools gave speeches, distributed declarations, and marched in formation along Daqiang Road, Hebei, North Road, and East Road, shouting slogans along the way. The police did not interfere, and the students also maintained order. Later, they turned to Riyi Road, Hebei, to petition the municipal government. Mayor Cheng Ke was ill in bed, and Secretary-General Sun Runyu rushed to receive the student representatives on his behalf. The student representatives jointly submitted a petition in the name of the Tianjin Municipal Petition Group of Middle Schools and Above, requesting the authorities for several points: Please forward to the Peiping authorities to speed up the release of arrested students. Please ask Song Zheyuan to abolish the puppet organization. Please ask the Peiping authorities to apologize to the students. Please pay medical expenses for the injured students. Guarantee all patriotic movements of the students. Remove the surveillance military and police from the colleges in Peiping and Tianjin. Sun Runyu replied that the presentation could be forwarded, but Mayor Cheng has been ordered to step down and the new Mayor Xiao has not taken office. Everything is difficult to manage, and I regret that I cannot be responsible for replying. I deeply hope that the students will understand this intention and stop this movement to avoid accidents. The representatives were satisfied and led the crowd to the public gymnasium, dispersing at about 11 am. The leaflets distributed during the parade and the slogans shouted were generally the same as the meaning of the presentation. (18th)

Sun Yat-sen University Students Hold Demonstration Parade; Guangzhou Student National Salvation Federation Holds Congress

Guangzhou Correspondence: Recently, students in Beiping staged a large-scale parade, but were dispersed by the Beiping authorities, and their representatives were arrested. National Economic Commission's Plan to Improve Anhui Tea 102

Qimen Tea Farm to Complete Purchase of New Machines for Grading Experiment Next Spring

Wuhu Correspondence: The southwestern counties of Anhui Province have traditionally been tea-producing areas. Western Anhui is known for its green tea, while Qimen in southern Anhui is renowned for its black tea. The total annual export volume is seven to eight million dan, with a value of tens of millions of yuan, which is of great importance to the rural economy. In the past, sales to foreign countries were insufficient to meet demand. However, due to poor production methods, in recent years, they have been affected by the competitive sales of tea from Japan, India, and Java. In foreign markets, they have been completely encroached upon. The National Economic Commission believes that improving Anhui tea is an important task for increasing production. It has jointly agreed with the Ministry of Industry, the Anhui Provincial Government, to reorganize the existing tea experiment farm in Qimen. The purpose is to improve Qimen tea through technical research. According to the Anhui Construction Department, the farm is currently managed by the Qimen Office of the Agricultural Department of the National Economic Commission. The internal organization of the office is divided into two sections: General Affairs and Technology. The Technology Section is divided into Tea Improvement Farm, Cooperative Promotion, Trainee, Packaging Improvement, Qimen Hospital, Grading Experiment, and Mechanical Experiment Factory. The various farms and offices have a total of seven or eight rooms, which is a large scale. The newly established Qimen Hospital and Tea Chemistry Laboratory are located in Rao Ci, Raoshanwu, with the tea-making chemistry laboratory adjacent to it. The machinery was recently purchased from Shanghai and transported to Qimen. Workers are already engaged in tea-making and using machinery for grading chemistry experiments to seek progress in production methods. The new farm address on Phoenix Mountain is currently under construction and is expected to be completed in March next year. A winter cooperative tea-making training class has also been opened to recruit tea farmers near Qimen to provide simple training. In addition, one or two trainees from each county of Guichi, Shitai, and Zhizhi are sent to Qimen for training. At the same time, cooperation is promoted, long-term tea loans are made, and a film is produced to be shown in various villages to arouse farmers to unanimously improve tea and increase production. (December 19th)

Tomb of Bian Dashou of the Ming Dynasty Robbed; Losses Exceed One Million 103

Treasures All Looted, Scattered Bones, Descendant Bian Ziqing Visits Yutian

Beiping Correspondence: Bian Dashou, a prominent official of the Ming Dynasty, along with Wu Sangui and others, were important figures in the north at the time. After Bian's death, he was buried in Yutian, Hebei. The jewels in his tomb were numerous, comparable to the Eastern Tombs of Malanyu. Since the Eastern Tombs robbery, tombs of value in Hebei have often been robbed. However, Bian Dashou's tomb was carefully protected and only recently was robbed by bandits. The details are as follows:

Tomb Architecture

Bian Dashou, a prominent official of the Ming Dynasty, along with Zu Dashou, Mao Wenlong, Wu Sangui, Hong Chengchou, and others, were famous figures in the north at the time. Bian served as Minister of Personnel and Grand Secretary in the Ming Dynasty and died in Pingdong at the age of eighty-nine. His descendants multiplied, and his family was wealthy. Many of them served as officials in the early Qing Dynasty. He was buried in the second district of Yutian County, about two li west of Zhang Hongqiao, in the northeast of Dadafeng Village, Hedong. There were more than two hundred tombs of various sizes, with towering steles and ancient cypresses. The tomb was surrounded by walls made of tiger skin stone, marble, and white marble. Successors continued to build it, making it majestic and magnificent, known far and wide, and one of the most valuable historical sites in the history of Pingxi. According to the locals, every tomb in the cemetery contained treasures, comparable in value to the Eastern Tombs of Malanyu. However, due to its solid construction and many tomb keepers, and the local Public Security Bureau repeatedly sending police to protect it, it was difficult for bandits to succeed.

Robbery Process

According to Bian Ziqing, a descendant of Bian, upon returning to Ping, he stated that recently, the police at the cemetery were withdrawn. On the night of the early tenth of this month (6th), at 12:00 p.m., thirty to forty tomb robbers suddenly arrived with pistols, knives, iron picks, lanterns, torches, and ropes. They stormed into the home of the tomb keepers and tied up Shi Youfa, Shi Lianfang, and other father and son, and confined the women, the old and the weak in the Shi family in the house, stuffing their mouths with cloth and cotton. They immediately went to the tomb and began digging, completely digging through Bian Dashou's tomb and three tombs on either side. They dug all night until dawn before finishing the digging and leaving with shouts. After dawn, a passerby heard the voices of people in the yard and entered to release the bound and confined Shis. Shi Youfa and others rushed to Beiping that day to report the incident to me. Upon hearing the news, I went to investigate. Upon arriving at the tomb, I saw the ancestral coffin thrown on the ground, and the bones were scattered everywhere. In addition to quickly sending someone to Ping to prepare a new coffin to be transported to Yutian for reburial, I inspected each tomb according to the family tree. I heard that Bian Dashou's tomb was missing a Ming Dynasty imperial sword called the Azure Dragon Sword, worth 500,000 yuan; a pearl called the Water-Repelling Pearl, worth 300,000 yuan. Besides the one stored in the Forbidden City, whose whereabouts are unknown, there is a town sea bell with a pearl beneath it. In total, there are only three pearls, each about the size of a table tennis ball, that can repel water. In addition, there were dozens of scattered pearls of various sizes in the tomb, worth more than one million yuan in total. All of them have been lost. In addition to submitting a report to the county government, a request has also been submitted to the Hebei provincial government to issue a notice to investigate the bandits and the whereabouts of the treasures. (December 18th)

Farmers in Fengjing, Chaowu Township, Songjiang, Robbed 104

Fengjing, Chaowu Township: The home of Jin Shangen, a villager in Bao Qi Jia, was suddenly robbed the night before last. The bandits pried open a hole in the wall and entered, threatening the owner with sharp knives. They robbed him of twenty yuan in banknotes, a gold ring, a silver lock, rice, cloth, and other items, and fled with their loot. The villagers have submitted a list of losses and reported the incident to the police for investigation.

Suzhou: Township Business Corps Continue Defense as Usual 105

Due to the provincial order for reorganization, the business corps in the city and townships of Wu County, except for some branches bordering Taihu Lake and the bustling areas of the city, which continue to be on duty for local security reasons, most branches have been suspended invisibly. Recently, the provincial order allowed them to pass the winter defense period and then reorganize. Therefore, as of the 20th, except for the 3rd, 15th, and 10th departments in the urban area, which have not been on duty for various reasons, all other branches have been on duty. All 18 branches in the township area have been on duty to maintain winter security. The necessary expenses, in addition to subsidies from the County Chamber of Commerce, are still raised locally by each branch.

Wuxi: County Agricultural Warehouse Established Today 106

The Wuxi County Agricultural Warehouse Management Committee held a committee meeting in the county government on the 19th, chaired by County Chief Long. It was resolved that the county's agricultural warehouse, which had been ordered to be established repeatedly, would be set up first in Sitou as the main warehouse and Youjiatan as the branch warehouse, and it would be opened on the 21st. The loan contract will be set at 30,000 yuan for a term of nine months and will be repaid in full. * Dongsheng Yongfeng Pawnshop, which is very close to the Provincial Agricultural Bank's Dongting Warehouse, should follow the county's regulations and unified methods, and no storage and pawn institutions should be added within ten li. The pawnshop has been closed for many years, but this year it suddenly resumed business, which is not conducive to the unified method. The meeting sent a letter to advise it to stop. * All pawnshops, banks, and warehouses that also operate agricultural warehouses should apply for registration. The meeting sent a letter to the Chamber of Commerce to advise them. Other matters were briefly discussed.

Nantong: Commissioner Xu Inspects Township Self-Defense 107

There are occasional bandits sneaking into the counties under Tong jurisdiction to cause disturbances. The commissioner's office specially ordered the county chiefs to order all townships to select able-bodied men to form patrol teams. Commissioner Xu Zhen, in order to understand the implementation situation, went to the counties overnight with Chief of Staff Peng Long and scientist Jia Zongfu to inspect. Those who have not yet formed teams are required to complete the task within five days.

Sir, since the crisis in North China and the patriotic movement of students in Beiping on the 9th of this month, our association immediately responded. However, in the past ten days, all telegrams, declarations, and communications from students in Hangzhou have not been sent out. Regarding what Education Minister Wang said in his speech on the 19th, "If students have opinions on political current events, there are legitimate ways to express them," it is difficult to apply to Hangzhou students. Our association, considering that the situation is getting more difficult and that the Beiping students are bleeding for the patriotic cause, and there is no way to express legitimate opinions, specially instructed someone to bring this letter to Shanghai for publication, so that the patriotic enthusiasm of tens of thousands of young people in Hangzhou and their determination to support the Beiping students can be fully expressed to the people of the country. Thank you very much. Sincerely, Student Union of National Zhejiang University, December 20, 24.

Major Middle and University Students in This City Petitioned to the City Government Yesterday; Gathered and Paraded the Night Before Last; Arrived at the City Government Early Yesterday Morning; Mayor Wu and Director Pan and Others Received Them Separately; Students Felt Satisfied and Were Sent Back by Car 109

Since the Shanghai student patriotic movement began, all actions have been orderly. After the petition of Fudan University students to the city government at 2:00 p.m. the day before yesterday, others such as Jinan University, Jiaotong University, Fudan University, Datong University, Guanghua University, Chizhi University, Shanghai University, Datong University, Zhengfeng University, Law School, Tongji University, Tongde University, Southeast Medical University, Law and Political Science, and other universities, McLaren, Nanyang Model, Jinan University Affiliated Middle School, Shizhong, Guanghua Affiliated Middle School, Jingye, Wuben, Southeast, Liangjiang, Yuqing, Fudan University Affiliated Middle School, Shizhong, Shanghai University Affiliated Middle School, Datong Middle School, China Middle School, Datong Middle School, Minli, Minli Girls' Middle School, China Girls' Middle School, Guangxia, Ai Qun, Yue Dong, Guangdong, Nanyang, Datong, Ai Guo, Junyi, East Asia, Qingxin Boys' Middle School, Qingxin Boys' Middle School, Qingxin Girls' Middle School, Jiangxi Vocational School, and other middle and high school students and representatives, a total of more than 6,000 people, started to contact each other from 4:00 p.m. the day before yesterday (19th) and gathered at Jiaotong University for a meeting. They elected a presidium to lead them. At about 9:00 p.m. that night, they departed from Jiaotong University in a line and followed Zhongshan Road and Shuodian Road. At about 3:00 a.m. yesterday, they arrived at Fudan University. After a short rest, they continued to advance towards the city center, arriving at the city government at around 5:30 a.m. The city government had received the news in advance and sent personnel to take care of them along the way. Considering that the students had been walking for a long distance all night, they prepared bread and tea for the students to eat. Mayor Wu and others arrived at the city government at dawn and personally received the students in front of the stone steps of the city government. When the students saw Mayor Wu, they all applauded and cheered. Mayor Wu expressed his condolences and earnestly persuaded the students to maintain strict discipline and order in the patriotic movement to avoid causing other disputes and increasing the government's difficulties. At the same time, he hoped that the students would not abandon their studies because of the patriotic movement. After listening to Mayor Wu's speech, the students were deeply moved and submitted a written request from the student presidium: * Request the mayor to telegram the central government to stop the North China military and political authorities from suppressing the students' patriotic movement. * Request the government to send troops immediately to suppress the rebel Yin Rugeng. * Request the government to preserve the integrity of the country's territory and sovereignty. * Request the government to implement an active revolutionary diplomacy. * Request the mayor to immediately release Li Zhensheng, a student of Jiaotong University who was arrested. * Request the mayor to protect the patriotic movement in Shanghai. * Request the government to guarantee freedom of speech and assembly. Mayor Wu immediately replied that he would do his best to protect the patriotic movement in Shanghai within the scope of maintaining discipline and order. As for Li Junsheng, he was not arrested. He was taken to the Public Security Bureau for questioning because a letter was found that was suspected of being suspicious. After the questioning, he was released back to the school and it had nothing to do with the patriotic movement. As for the other requests, Mayor Wu promised to forward them to the central government. All the students were satisfied with the reply and dispersed with cheers. It was already about 9:00 a.m. Because it was raining and the road was far, the city government prepared dozens of large group cars to send the students back to school. It was found that the more than 5,000 students who participated in this petition were representatives of major middle and high schools in the city. Students who did not participate continued to attend classes as usual. All representatives of the schools who participated in the petition returned to school and continued to attend classes as usual. All schools in the city did not suspend classes.

Meeting of School Representatives

In order to support the patriotic movement of students in Beiping, all students in Shanghai first gathered at Jinan University at 4:00 p.m. the day before yesterday, together with more than 5,000 students from schools such as Datong, Guanghua, Jiaotong, Chizhi, and Law School, and Nanyang Model Middle School. At 3:00 a.m. yesterday morning, they gathered at Fudan University and convened a temporary meeting of representatives from various schools in the library of the school. Each school sent five representatives to form the presidium. From the five representatives, one chief representative was elected from each school. A total of 79 representatives from schools such as Jinan, Datong, Guanghua, Jiaotong, Chizhi, Law School, Fudan, Nanyang Model Middle School, Liangjiang, Dongwu, Tongde, Law and Politics, Shanghai Medical College, Tax College, Yuqing Middle School, China Middle School, Fudan Shizhong, etc., Shen Yiwei, Hu Yining, Zheng Xuanzhi, Wei Dingyi, Zhang Yanqing, and other representatives. At that time, a temporary chairman, Jinan, and a temporary recorder, Chizhi, were elected. Seven points were resolved to petition to Mayor Wu (details omitted in another draft). After the discussion, the team was organized at 4:00 a.m., and the whole team set off to the city government at 5:30 a.m. They arrived in front of the city government gate. Then Mayor Wu came out of the city government courtyard and answered the crowd. The students felt satisfied, and the team returned to school at 10:00 a.m.

Second Batch Arrived; More Than 1,000 People

At 9:30 a.m., more than 1,000 students from more than ten schools, including Zhengfeng Middle School, Yuqing Middle School, Datong University, Datong Affiliated Middle School, Fudan Shiyan Middle School, Tongde Medical College, Guangxia Middle School, McLaren Skin, etc., continued to arrive at the city government. Director Pan gave separate answers. However, the students still requested Pan to reply in writing. Director Pan accepted the request and gave a written reply. The students felt satisfied. At 2:30 p.m., a part of more than 200 people organized a team and left the city government and returned on foot, and the rest also dispersed one after another.

Since the purpose of your petition is the same as that of the petition delegation in the morning, he would tell them in detail Mayor Wu's answers to the requests of the petition delegation in the morning. The students felt satisfied and dispersed with cheers. The city government prepared 20 group cars to send the students back to school.

At 10:00 a.m. yesterday, when students from various schools were petitioning at the city government, students from various schools in South Shanghai also made a move to parade in the rain. It has been found that the more than 5,000 students who participated in this petition were representatives of major middle and high schools in the city.
