Mayor Wu's Letter to All Students in the City 110

Mayor Wu yesterday issued a letter to all students in the city, saying: In recent days, thousands of students from major middle and high schools in this city have come to the government to petition because they are worried about the national crisis. We deeply sympathize with the expression of this patriotic spirit, and most of them are disciplined and orderly, and they can still avoid the mistakes of strikes and riots in the past. We are especially gratified. However, because there are many people and the road is long, the representatives of the schools are in the middle of winter, from night to dawn, and they have traveled a long distance. In addition to admiring their patriotic enthusiasm, we are also deeply uneasy. Seeing this phenomenon, Tiecheng is restless in the bedroom, and he is always concerned about the safety and homework of the young students in the city. However, at this time, Tiecheng is for the sake of protecting the youth and for the sake of the youth to whom the life of the nation is tied. There are still things that cannot be said. I would like to express my sincerity and hope to learn from it together.

China is unfortunate to encounter this national crisis, but the arrival of the national crisis is not a matter of one morning and one evening, but a result of the accumulation of historical and global long-term and complex causes. Therefore, saving the country and seeking survival is the most difficult and serious work in the world, and the nation must make efforts on its own, each in its own position, to cultivate the potential of the country's life. What we should learn from the country is not a temporary impulse, not a temporary indignation, but a determination and perseverance to fight and work hard for the country forever.

The central government has already made a prudent decision on the entire diplomatic policy, and the responsible authorities have also repeatedly declared that the government is deeply concerned about the importance of national affairs, the situation in North China, and the necessity of maintaining sovereignty and territory, and is working hard to deal with them. They will never shirk the responsibilities that should be assumed, and they will never give up the rights and interests that should be maintained. However, due to the deep weakness of the nation, it has not been possible to break through this difficult and difficult environment immediately. The people of the country should painfully encourage themselves, swear their sincerity and contribute their strength, and take the spirit of helping each other in the same boat, and vow to be the backing of the government and the country, so that the central authorities can more effectively cope with this dangerous situation.

The city government has forwarded the opinions of the students in this city to the central government. All our young people can only be moved by their hearts, be patient, and maintain a calm spirit and attitude to help the central government cope, and do not take a temporary anger, do not make false and reckless actions, turn the government's energy, and increase the difficulties of the authorities.

Tiecheng loves the country and dares not be behind others. However, there is an undeniable weakness in the patriotic movements of the past, that is, taking the surface for the actual, taking the means for the purpose, so that abandoning the fundamentals and chasing the ends, using energy in vain, not enough to succeed, but more than enough to spoil things. This is the crux of the failure of the national liberation movement over the years, and the reason why China's national spirit is strong on the outside and weak on the inside and cannot help foreign countries, or even be used by a few people with ulterior motives. This is a dangerous step. After Germany's disastrous defeat in 1806, its patriotic philosopher Fichte once frankly warned his people: "Germany's defeat today is caused by the various diseases of the entire German people in peacetime. The future war is a war of character, a war of morality, and a war of knowledge." My enlightened youth in the city, if you forget the precedent of Germany's revival, please remember this philosopher's advice and do not strike, but devote your energy to preparing for the "war of knowledge" with your teeth clenched, to win the final victory for our nation, and to ensure and promote the independent and unshakable life of our nation for thousands of years. December 20, 24.

Cunninghame Departs Shanghai This Morning to Return Home: Enthusiastic Farewell from All Sides Yesterday Afternoon Before Embarkation. Before the Arrival of the New Consul-General Gauss, Twiss Will Act as Chargé d'Affaires. 116

Mr. Cunninghame, the retiring U.S. Consul-General in Shanghai, embarked on the Dollar Steamship Company's President Lincoln at 2:30 PM yesterday and set sail at 2:00 AM this morning, departing Shanghai to return to the United States. More than one hundred people from various Chinese and foreign circles went to the pier yesterday for an enthusiastic farewell. The details are as follows:

Departure Situation

The ship was docked between the 12th and 13th pontoons on the Huangpu River. It was scheduled to set sail at 4:00 AM this morning. Mr. Cunninghame moved from his official residence inside the U.S. Consulate to the Cathay Hotel on the Bund of Nanjing Road the day before yesterday to facilitate farewells from all sides. Therefore, he boarded the ship in advance at 2:30 PM yesterday afternoon. At that time, all the farewell personnel had gathered at the Nanjing Road Bund pier. A detachment of U.S. Marine Corps honor guards and a full military band were specially dispatched to line up on the lawn in front of the pier to wait to pay their respects. Mr. Cunninghame drove to the pier, reviewed the honor guards, shook hands and exchanged greetings with each of the farewell personnel, and then boarded the U.S. Navy Ashevill small boat amidst the melodious music and departed from the port.

Farewell Personnel

Those who went to the pier to bid farewell at that time included Yu Hongjun, the Secretary-General representing Mayor Wu Tiecheng of the city; Yu Ming, the Director of the Foreign Ministry's Shanghai Office; Zheng Lai, the Commissioner of Customs; the consular corps leader, Norwegian Consul-General in Shanghai, Røer; British Consul Bevir; French Consul Patras; Russian Consul Spivana; Japanese Consul Ishishe; Italian Consul Nillon; German Consul Kriebel; Belgian Consul Thamls; Dutch Consul Bottevein; Cuban Consul-General Massill; Czech Consul-General Markesh; Danish Consul-General Schiøler; Spanish Consul-General Furey; Mexican Consul-General Filisco; Portuguese Consul-General Alves; British Commercial Counselor George; Fessenden, Director-General of the Public Works Department; and U.S. Acting Consul-General Twiss, Hill, a Chinese provincial judge, Commander of the Marine Corps, Franklin, President of the Chamber of Commerce, and more than one hundred American community representatives, including Mr. Cunninghame's friends.

Remarks Before Departure

When Mr. Cunninghame left Shanghai yesterday, he wore a regular suit, covered with a dark blue cashmere overcoat, and black leather shoes. He was in high spirits. He told the reporter of the New Voice News Agency that he had been in China for many years and was quite reluctant to say goodbye now. He hoped that if there was an opportunity, he could come to China again. Mr. Cunninghame's wife passed away in Shanghai in the year before last. He is traveling alone on this trip. Mr. Cunninghame was born in eastern Tennessee. He first arrived in Shanghai on September 8, 1919. He has served in China for a total of 22 years, and has held the position of Consul-General in Shanghai for as long as 16 years. His relationship with all parties is very harmonious, and he has made many contributions to Sino-American relations.

[Image: Mr. Cunninghame (right) with those who bid farewell (Photo by Qichang)]

Gauss

According to news from the U.S. Consulate, Mr. Gauss, the newly appointed Consul-General in Shanghai, who is currently the Consul-General in Paris, France, is still in Paris and is scheduled to first go to the United States before bringing his family to China. He is expected to arrive in Shanghai and take up his duties in the consular district around the end of February next year. In the meantime, Mr. Twiss will act as Chargé d'Affaires with full authority.

The Ministry of Finance Actively Prepares to Establish a Real Estate Mortgage Bank; The National Products Factory Federation Received a Reply from the Ministry of Finance Yesterday 119

The Shanghai National Products Factory Federation previously submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance on the 2nd of this month to stabilize exchange rates and establish a real estate mortgage bank to provide relief, due to the economic downturn and the decline of various industries. The Federation received a reply from the Ministry of Finance yesterday, Qian Zi No. 8129, stating: "The letter presented on October 2nd, 24th year of the Republic, expressing extreme support for the new monetary policy, and submitting six proposed opinions for review and implementation, has been fully received, along with the accompanying memorandum. The Preparatory Committee for the Issuance of Banknotes already has representatives from all sectors participating, and branch associations have been established in Guangzhou, Wuhan, Tianjin, Jinan, etc. As for the request to have local industrial and commercial associations organize price stabilization committees, the Ministry will issue orders to handle this as necessary. The prohibition of unscrupulous merchants from manipulating and devaluing legal tender is clearly stipulated in Article 7 of the Measures for the Exchange of Legal Tender, and the Ministry has issued orders to the provincial and municipal governments to handle this accordingly. The Ministry is actively preparing for the encouragement of auxiliary currency use and the establishment of a real estate mortgage bank. The stabilization of exchange rates has also been entrusted to the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications by the Ministry through letters to handle this properly. You are hereby informed of this." This is the reply.

Jiangsu Sericulture Improvement Association Negotiates Silkworm Seed Loan; 160,000 Yuan Has Been Principally Agreed Upon 120

Since the silk industry shows signs of improvement and silk prices have soared, silk factories in Shanghai, Wuxi, and other places have been forced to suspend production due to a shortage of raw materials. The Zhejiang Provincial Sericulture and Silk Control Committee established a spring silkworm seed loan of 200,000 yuan with the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications. Now, the Jiangsu Provincial Sericulture Improvement Management Committee is also negotiating a spring silkworm seed loan of 160,000 yuan with the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Shanghai China Industrial Bank, and the Jiangsu Farmers' Bank. The Association has already negotiated with the Zhenjiang branch of the six banks. The principle has been agreed upon, and the contract will be signed after the Zhenjiang branches of each bank telegraph Shanghai headquarters for approval. The term is said to be one year, with an interest rate of one percent per month.

The guild will hold an executive committee meeting today to organize guild affairs. All industries are safely weathering the year-end period, and there are no other concerns. The details are as follows:

At the same time, it has been decided to hold another executive committee meeting at 5:00 PM this afternoon (Saturday) to organize the guild affairs report for the general meeting of members. As for the savings departments of various banks, they began closing their accounts on the 15th, and the business departments began closing their accounts yesterday. Staff members of various banks have not been allowed to take leave unless absolutely necessary in recent days, and are very busy handling account closing matters. Internal office hours are extended depending on the account closing situation of each bank.

Money Exchanges: The general account closing period for members of the Money Exchanges Association for the 24th year of the Republic has been internally set for January 23rd and will be announced after approval by the executive committee meeting on the 24th of this month. However, due to the approaching account closing period for banks in the second half of the year, all exchanges and the Joint Reserve Treasury of Money Exchanges are prepared. Although the spot exchange rate for silver in the money market yesterday was still one jiao, the receipt and disbursement of funds between silver and money exchanges were busier than in the past. Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau Deposits Cash Reserves into the Treasury 122

Four Provisional Measures Prescribed; A Circular Order to All Bureaus to Comply

Since the Ministry of Finance announced the new monetary policy implementing state ownership of cash reserves, the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau in this city has specially stipulated the following four provisional measures: All cash reserves of all branch bureaus and postal districts should be sealed immediately, and the amount of deposits should be telegraphed to the Bureau; Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications banknotes approved by the Ministry of Finance should be used for paying deposits and remittances; International drafts should be handled according to the exchange rates indicated by the Central Bank; In case the funds of a branch bureau are insufficient to pay, it can contact the three banks at any time to borrow, etc. These measures have been circulated to all branch bureaus for compliance. Subsequently, payments for savings, remittances, etc., will be made in legal tender. After receiving the order, all bureaus have complied and have transferred the sealed cash reserves to the General Bureau one after another. The General Bureau remitted all of them to the Central Bank last week.

Organizational Outline

Organizational Outline of the Shanghai "National Products Year and National Products Games for Citizens": This association is named the "Shanghai National Products Year Committee for Citizens" based on the meaning of designating national products as the theme of the year over the years; The purpose of this association is to awaken the national patriotic spirit of Shanghai citizens, awaken the people of the whole country to use national products, seek production and sales cooperation, and strive to promote national products; The association will establish a temporary office within the Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Joint Association; The association is jointly organized by various legal national products organizations in Shanghai; The association will establish a board of supervisors and a board of directors. There is no fixed number of directors and supervisors, who will be elected by the representatives' assembly of national products organizations; The association will have 21 standing directors elected by the directors, and seven departments for secretary, general affairs, finance, organization, publicity, compilation, and investigation, with one director and one deputy director for each department; The standing directors of the association will elect one chairman and one vice-chairman to preside over the association's affairs internally and represent the association externally; For the sake of popularizing publicity, the association will also organize a design committee and a publicity committee. The method of their formation is the same as the election of directors, but it is not limited to representatives of organizations; The association may, if necessary, appoint honorary directors with the approval of the board of directors; For the needs of handling affairs, the association may hire staff and organize a staff department, acting under the will of the standing directors and serving the association exclusively; The articles of association for the association's board of directors and various committees, and the publicity outline, will be formulated separately; Matters not fully covered in this outline may be amended by the board of directors.

Implementation Measures

Measures for holding the "National Products Year for Citizens" on New Year's Day in the 25th year of the Republic: Issue a declaration; Issue a letter to the citizens; Announce a city-wide business shutdown for one day; Broadcast on the radio, promoting the consumption of national products; Various amusement parks will stage patriotic plays promoting the consumption of national products; Automobiles, bicycles, and various vehicles will hold parades and lantern festivals; Post slogans; Newspapers will publish special editions; Issue badges for the "National Products Year for Citizens"; Hold national products games ("opening in the morning, entertainment in the afternoon"); Hold a national products exhibition, exclusively for exhibition and not for selling goods.

Ministry of Finance: Affirms That Delivery Notes Should Have Stamps 129

Invoices Without Prices Are Exempt

The Ministry of Finance replied to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce regarding the request from the Shanghai Pharmaceutical Industry Association to exempt three types of goods invoices from stamp duty. The reply stated: Both the telegram and attachments are noted. Upon investigation, when goods are sold and an invoice containing the name, quantity, or price of the goods is issued, it constitutes a sales invoice. The delivery notes used by the pharmaceutical industry, since they contain the name and quantity of the goods and are issued with the goods, even without a price, should still have stamps affixed according to the regulations for sales invoices. Although it is claimed that the notes clearly state "a formal invoice will be provided upon acceptance," implying that another invoice will be issued, it is apparent that there will not be inspection personnel present at every transaction to verify this. Therefore, it cannot be proven. Regarding the delivery notes from Tongmaoyuan and Laiyuan stores that were fined, the word "entered" is already written on the notes, indicating that the goods have been sold. It is reasonable to assume that the business would issue another invoice at the same time as delivering the goods. However, if the purchaser relies on the delivery note for accounting purposes, why not mark "entered" on the invoice containing the price instead of the delivery note, which is only for viewing samples? This clearly indicates that the claim that a separate invoice will be issued after the transaction is a deceptive practice. Furthermore, purchasers have no use for unsold delivery notes and therefore do not need to keep them. If a separate invoice is used for settled transactions, it does not need to be saved. Therefore, since these delivery notes were confiscated, there is no doubt that they are disguised invoices. The request for exemption from stamp duty is denied. As for account statements used for reconciliation, they refer to statements issued to clients at the end of each month or year to verify whether the amounts paid and received are correct. These statements should be limited to those that list the amounts paid and received before the end of the month or year. If the account statements used by the pharmaceutical industry only list the names and quantities of the medicines received and paid, with the dates of receipt and payment clearly indicated, but without the prices, these types of statements can be exempted from stamp duty according to the law. The reason is that when the other party records the medicines, they will definitely be entered into their account books. Therefore, it is not necessary to list them again when issuing the monthly statement for reconciliation. If the price is also listed, it is no different from an invoice for payment as described in item three of the tax schedule and cannot be regarded as an account statement for reconciliation. Please instruct them to comply accordingly. This is the approved reply.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Sends a Telegram to the Jiangxi Provincial Government Expressing Gratitude for the Cancellation of the Porcelain Industry Extermination Donation 132

And Requests Earnest Protection for National Porcelain

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Jiangxi Provincial Government yesterday, stating: "To Chairman Xiong of the Jiangxi Provincial Government in Nanchang: According to a report from the local porcelain industry association, the one-year term for the temporary subsidy donation for the extermination of bandits by merchants in Jingdezhen has expired. We have received your government's order to cancel the donation as scheduled and change it to a business tax. Your government's trustworthiness and care for merchants is admired. Upon hearing this news, porcelain merchants are grateful, believing that this is a turning point for the better. Porcelain is a special product of Jiangxi Province. In recent years, it has been severely affected by bandit activities and foreign products, causing business to decline sharply. Without earnest protection, it will be difficult to recover. According to the Business Tax Law passed by the Legislative Yuan and promulgated by the National Government, business tax is levied on stores, not on forwarding merchants. Some officials in various provinces may not fully understand this point, resulting in a disguised form of transit tax. There have been cases where merchants have petitioned the Ministry of Finance to correct this in accordance with the law. We propose that your government instruct the relevant departments to pay attention to this, so that the export of porcelain products will not be obstructed along the way. We respectfully offer this suggestion in the hope that it will be adopted. Sincerely, Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce."

Accused of Deliberately Embezzling Estate Under Management; Xie Lianqing is Sued 141

Discovered After Inspecting Accounts; Zhang Wu Sues

The rich merchant from Ningbo, Zhang Yanzhong, who lived in Shanghai, established the Hengchangxiang Machinery Shipbuilding Factory in Hongkou. The business was unusually prosperous. Unfortunately, in September of the Republic of China's 15th year, Zhang Yanzhong suddenly fell ill and died, leaving behind a large estate. Because his only son was young, relatives and friends from the same hometown organized the Zhang Xiarang Estate Management Committee and publicly elected Xie Lianqing as the chairman. He resided in the factory, and all the property was under Xie Lianqing's control. Last year, Zhang's wife, Zhang Wu, discovered that various businesses were facing financial difficulties. She entrusted accountant Huang Bingzhang to audit the accounts. In April of the same year, Xie and others handed over the managed property. It was then that Xie Lianqing's deliberate embezzlement of the estate under management was discovered. Zhang Wu hired lawyers Peng Yuanxun and Xiang Xun to file a private prosecution in the criminal division of the local court, stating that the defendant, Xie Lianqing, had deliberately betrayed his friendship for personal gain. He used his power as manager to sell the five mu, three fen, five li, and four hao of land on East Broadway Road without authorization. According to the accountant's report, there was a discrepancy of 64,266 taels of silver. Furthermore, when the Municipal Council acquired one mu, eight fen, three li, and four hao of land for road expansion, it allocated 66,000 taels of silver as compensation for the land price. This was not recorded in the accounts, and it is unknown who used the money. There were many buildings and houses on the land, with an annual rental income of more than 15,000 yuan. Even if the buildings were demolished and sold as waste materials, there should have been some income. However, after a thorough search of the accounts, there was no record of it at all. How did the defendant dispose of it? After the accountant inquired with the defendant, they refused to answer, causing the plaintiff great losses. To cite just one of the largest amounts, the defendant has clearly committed crimes under Article 342 and Article 335 of the Criminal Law. A request is made to investigate and punish him, so that the evil practice of deceiving orphans and the weak in society can be punished, and a civil lawsuit is also attached. After receiving the complaint, the court held a special hearing in the third courtroom at 10:00 AM yesterday, presided over by Judge Chen Jingyi. The plaintiff, Zhang Wu, and lawyers Peng and Xiang were present in court. The defendant, Xie Lianqing, also hired lawyers Wang Jianhang and others to appear in court to defend him. First, Zhang Wu testified that she was 53 years old, from Ningbo, and lived at No. 2 Tangshan Road. She also recounted the previous events and stated that after her husband died, the defendants organized the Estate Management Committee. Last year, when the factory was reorganized, she refused to sign, and the accountant was hired to audit the accounts and found discrepancies. The defendant's lawyer stated that the defendant was old and appeared in court with illness, and requested permission to be seated. The judge granted permission. The defendant, Xie Lianqing, sat and testified that he was 68 years old, from Zhenhai, Zhejiang, and lived at No. 1 Qing'an Lane, Guangqi Road, in Shanghai City. He stated that it was his own property, that he used to be in the money industry, and that he was now retired at home due to old age. He confirmed that after Zhang Yanzhong died, the Estate Management Committee was organized, consisting of seven people, including himself. When asked if there were management regulations, he replied no. When asked if he was in charge of everything and should therefore be responsible, and who sold the land privately, he replied that it was sold by one of the six people, and he did not know. He requested that Yuan be summoned because Yuan was a relative of the plaintiff. The judge obtained this information and stated that the case still required witnesses to be summoned. Lawyer Peng stated that the civil lawsuit in this case was significant and requested that the defendant be detained or provide a guarantee of 100,000 yuan from a reliable shop. The judge then ordered that the defendant not be detained in consideration of his old age and illness, but that a guarantee should be arranged, and instructed the lawyers of both parties to try to settle the civil lawsuit out of court. After the instructions were given, the court adjourned.

Japanese Smuggling Silver 144

According to the French Shanghai Daily, translated by the Foreign Press, when the President Truman ship was leaving the port the other day, several Chinese customs officers boarded the ship to inspect it and paid particular attention to searching Japanese people for silver. At that time, there were indeed several Japanese people on board who were planning to smuggle silver out of the country. When the customs officers came to check, they were forced to come up with a plan. One of them took out 3,000 silver dollars and threw them onto the Central Wharf. At that time, there were many coolies working on the wharf. When the sound of the silver coins hitting the ground was heard, they scattered like birds and beasts and rushed to grab the silver dollars. Because the silver coins were scattered, it was not easy to gather the coolies together for a while. The customs officers were very surprised to see this situation and assumed that the Japanese had already disposed of the smuggled goods, so they stopped checking and left. But in fact, more than sixty Japanese people on board were carrying huge amounts of silver coins and took advantage of the customs officers' confusion to leave the port safely.

In order to further his studies, he also studies English at night at an English night school set up by four people in the Zhonghua Building. His parents found out about this and felt that marriage was not a child's play and that a matchmaker should be formally hired to negotiate. Xuejun learned of this and felt that his good intentions had gone wrong and his reputation was ruined. The date of his graduation from school was still far away, and there was no hope for marriage. Who knew that the defendant had ulterior motives and, seven or eight years ago, had the girl come to his house, enticing her with vanity. In recent years, Xingzhen's knowledge has gradually increased, and she has become literate and knows right from wrong. The daughter was now being sent over by Chinese and Western detectives. The plaintiff was heartbroken. She inquired at all the police stations and found that there was no such thing. It was clear that the defendant had lured her away. The plaintiff is not as wealthy as her biological father, but she has enough to eat three meals a day. Crows have a sense of gratitude, and cats and dogs have loyalty to their owners. Humans are not animals, so how can they be so ignorant of conscience and be tempted by vanity? The plaintiff has now learned that she is being hidden in his house. She has sent letters requesting her return, but to no avail. Therefore, she is suing him under Article 240 of the Criminal Law. The court issued a summons for both parties to be interrogated in the criminal court on the morning of yesterday. The plaintiff, Sun Yang, arrived in court with her lawyer and explained the situation, requesting an investigation. She asked that the defendant be ordered to return her daughter. The defendant, Yang Shaochen, stated that his daughter Xingzhen was born to him. Because her "eight characters" were not good and caused conflict, she was adopted by Sun Yang eleven days after birth. On the evening of the 16th of last month, a detective named Guan from the Laozha Police Station came and said, "Why don't you take your daughter back? She is being abused and forced to be a dancer and prostitute. If she is taken care of by me, she should be raised well, not treated as a cash cow." So, I took the daughter back. The girl then testified that her name was Yang Xingzhen, that she was sixteen years old, and that she lived at her father's house at No. 44 Belle Road. She was asked, "You were raised by Sun Yang, weren't you?" She replied, "Yes." She was asked, "Since Sun Yang raised you so well, why did you want to go back to your own home?" She replied, "Because I heard people say that I was going to be a dancer." She replied, "Because I heard that I was going to be a dancer, I left." The plaintiff then stated that Xingzhen had never been to the police station. She had inquired and found out that it was not true. Moreover, she had reported to the police station after Xingzhen ran away. The judge said to Ms. Yang, "Why don't you ask her father for some money? Besides, you will need money for your daughter's dowry when she gets married in the future." Ms. Yang replied, "I live for one person, I don't want money. Besides, I am already forty-one years old, and it is too late to have any more children." Battery Trademark Case, Court Hearing Concluded Yesterday, Verdict Next Friday 154

Hu Guoguang, owner of the China Battery Factory at No. 3, Yuqing Lane, Dongtangjia Alley, recently produced a kind of battery called the "Shu" brand. He applied for registration with the Trademark Bureau. After the Trademark Bureau examined and approved it, the Hezhong Electric Company believed that the sound of the China Battery Factory's "Shu" brand battery was the same as that of the company's registered "Mingzhu" brand battery. Yu Shu'an, chairman of the company (Chief Engineer of the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau of the Ministry of Communications), filed an objection. After deliberation by the Trademark Bureau, the objection was declared invalid and rejected. The company then filed a reconsideration, which has not yet been resolved. Yi Yixin, the business manager of Hezhong, filed a complaint with the First Special District Court against Hu Guoguang for fraud. The First Special Court had summoned him once. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Yang Qianchang held a hearing in the criminal court. Both parties were present. According to Zhang Yixin's statement, "Mingzhu" and "Shu" have the same pronunciation. In rural areas, people only know the sound and meaning and do not distinguish between the authenticity of the goods. Therefore, it has a significant impact on business and requested that the matter be handled according to law. The defendant's defending lawyer, E Sen, presented various documents from the Trademark Bureau to prove the facts of the case and said that before the administrative agency in charge of trademarks has made a decision, how can it be determined that the defendant's trademark is forged or original? Moreover, the plaintiff's objection has already been rejected. Therefore, this lawsuit is unfounded. It should be noted that the cause of this case is that the plaintiff applied to the Trademark Bureau to register the "Great Linked Beads" brand, which the defendant had been using for a long time, resulting in the Trademark Bureau rejecting the plaintiff's application. Therefore, this case is actually a means of retaliation. The court stated that the facts were clear and ordered the lawyers to begin their arguments. After the lawyers from both sides made their arguments, Judge Yang declared the hearing concluded and set a date for the verdict next Friday afternoon.

Zhongti Yueye Championship

Team and Individual Titles Both Go to Fushi

Zhu Wenzhang Finishes Full Course First at 14 Minutes 10 Seconds

Minli Temporarily Absent; Actually Only Three Schools Competed

The cross-country race organized by the Zhongxiao Sports Federation was held yesterday afternoon at 2:30 PM in drizzling rain. The entire course was 3,000 meters, with the starting and ending points both at the front of Fuzhong on Haig Road. A total of four schools, including Guanghua, Minli, Xunshi, and Fuzhong, registered for this year's event. Minli temporarily withdrew, and only three schools actually participated, with 26 athletes. As a result, Fushi won the championship with 46 points, Guanghua finished second with 54 points, and the third place went to Fuzhong. Zhu Wenzhang of Fushi also won the individual championship, achieving a time of 14 minutes and 10 seconds.

Zhu Wenzhang Emerges

At around 2:00 PM, 52 fast runners gathered in front of Fuzhong on Haig Road, and the race started at 2:30 PM, with Chen Bingde leading the way on a motorcycle. When passing Yidingpan Road, the racers gradually separated, with Zhu Wenzhang of Houshi spreading out his strides and emerging ahead. Wang Shijing of Guanghua followed closely. By the time they turned onto Baisai Zhong Road, they had already formed a long line. Due to the rain and slippery ground, the racers were extra careful. After crossing Zhu Erdian Road, half of the entire course had been covered. At the intersection of Fukaissen Road, Zhu Wenzhang was still leading the way, quickening his pace. Wang Shijing remained in second place, followed by Zheng of Fushi and Gao of Fuzhong, with the other racers not far behind. At this point, eight-tenths of the entire course had been covered, and all the leading racers were full of ambition. By the time they reached the intersection of Qiaoden Road and turned north onto Haig Road, the finish line was in sight. Zhu Wenzhang dashed forward like an arrow, breaking through and taking the lead, with a time of 14 minutes and 10 seconds. The second place went to Zheng Zhen of Fusai, and the third place went to Wang Shijing of Guanghua, with only a few steps separating them.

Fushi First in Team Event

After the race, Lu Xiangqian, Jiang Jingnan, Chen Bingde, and Han Kuiyong calculated the scores, taking the top six racers from each school. Fushi Zhongxiao won the championship with 46 points. Guanghua Middle School finished second with 54 points, and Fudan Middle School finished third with 73 points. It is a pity that Guanghua lost by eight points due to the absence of their strong athlete Zhang Heling. The results are as follows: 1. Zhu Wenzhang (Fushi); 2. Zheng Zhen (Fusai); 3. Wang Shijing (Guanghua); 4. Gao Jinfu (Fuzhong); 5. Chen Chongxian (Fuzhong); 6. Wen Yeping (Fushi); 7. Zhang Delin (Guanghua); 8. Zheng Shilu (Fusai); 9. Deng Tingkun (Guanghua); 10. Education News

Recent Education Situation in Guizhou Province

The estimated educational expenditure budget for Guizhou Province in the 24th year of the Republic is set at a total of 749,101.60 yuan, including expenses for the Department of Education, educational funds, special education for ethnic minorities, and expenses for the Tongzhi Museum and other cultural activities, accounting for 10.66% of the total provincial expenditure (7,029,468.84 yuan). The province has 36 secondary schools, normal schools, and vocational schools, including 10 provincial-level secondary schools (one for girls), 12 county-level secondary schools (three junior high schools for girls), 2 joint schools, and 5 private schools. There are 2 provincial-level normal schools (one for girls) and 4 county-level vocational schools. These schools have 1,629 students in senior high school (1,197 boys and 432 girls) and 7,491 students in junior high school (6,026 boys and 1,465 girls), totaling 9,120 students in both senior and junior high school. In addition, the province has one county-level girls' junior high school in Chishui County, which has not yet reported due to bandit activity this spring. There are also one boys' secondary school each in Meitan and Bijie and one girls' secondary school each in Qianxi and Dushan, which have not been approved by the Department of Education and are not included. Regarding vocational education, since the provincial-level vocational school was closed in 1927, only agricultural, industrial, and commercial courses have been offered within provincial-level senior high schools. In 1935, a provincial-level Guiyang junior vocational school was established with an opening budget of 25,000 yuan and a recurring expense of over 14,000 yuan. The three county-level secondary schools in Dading, Du, and Tianzhu Counties were renamed vocational schools and began recruiting junior vocational class students, with the province subsidizing each class 800 yuan annually. The total vocational education expenditure is 41,810.80 yuan, which is less than one-tenth of the allocated funding for secondary education (450,743.60 yuan). Although this does not meet the standards set by the Ministry of Education, it is a significant achievement considering that the province's vocational education has no foundation and is just beginning. The provincial authorities plan to gradually increase funding in the future.

Zhejiang Secondary School Graduation Examination

Decision to Hold Exams in Three Regions

Hangzhou, Jinhua, Taizhou

Starting January 7

The Zhejiang Province 24th Year First Semester Secondary School Graduation Examination Committee has decided to hold exams in the Hangzhou, Jinhua, and Taizhou regions due to the 1,196 graduating students from one senior high school and 33 junior high schools. The committee will hire examiners, invigilators, and other members to set the exam schedule and questions for each subject. The secondary school graduation examination for this year will be divided into three regions: (Region 1: Hangzhou Region) Provincial Hangzhou Senior High School, Provincial Hangzhou Girls' High School, Provincial Hangzhou Junior High School, Provincial Jiaxing Junior High School, Provincial Huzhou Junior High School, Provincial Ningbo Secondary School, Provincial Shaoxing Junior High School, Provincial Yanzhou Junior High School, Hangzhou Municipal Junior High School, Private Anding Junior High School, Private Zongwen Junior High School, Private Yanwu Junior High School, Private Mu Junior High School, Private Zhongshan Junior High School, Private Qinghua Junior High School, Private Hulin Junior High School, Private Shufan Junior High School, Private Huixing Girls' High School, Private Mingmin Girls' High School, Private Xingsu Girls' High School, Private Xiaoshi Secondary School, Private Jishan Secondary School, etc. Students from these 22 schools, totaling approximately 769 students (48 senior high school students and 721 junior high school students), will participate in this region. (Region 2: Taizhou Region) Provincial Taizhou Junior High School, Provincial Wenzhou Secondary School, Huangyan County Junior High School, Wenzhou Joint Junior High School, Ruian County Junior High School, Private Huipu Junior High School, Private Fuya Junior High School, etc. Students from these 7 schools, totaling 206 junior high school students, will participate in this region (no senior high school students). Opinions of Jiangsu Provincial Secondary School Principals on Visiting Education in North China

In order to encourage educational administrators in Jiangsu Province to improve their qualifications and to seek improvements in education in the province, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education has established regulations for educational administrators to visit education domestically and abroad. The department recently sent eight principals from the province to visit educational institutions in North China, including Zheng Xigu from Shangzhong, Peng Qinming from Changzhong, Liu Hengjing from Nanjing Girls' High School, Jiang Long from Private Girls' High School, Huang Dunfu from Qiling Xiang Teachers' School, Cao Yihua from Hai Teachers' School, Jin Shiru from Xu Girls' Teachers' School, and Zhang Yaomo from Suqian Vocational School. They traveled north from Nanjing on November 16, passing through cities and provinces such as Feng, Anji, Jinan, Doping, Qingdao, Tianjin, Beijing, Zhangjiakou, Baoding, Boye, Ding County, Taiyuan, Shijiazhuang, Zhengzhou, Kaifeng, and Xuzhou. They returned to Nanjing yesterday. A reporter interviewed Zheng Xigu, Huang Dunfu, and Liu Hengjing, representatives of the visiting group, inquiring about their experiences and materials collected during their visit to nine provinces and cities in North China, which lasted one month and two days. They stated that they had gained much from their personal development and that they had seen much that could be learned for the improvement of education in Jiangsu Province. The colleagues summarized their observations as follows:

A. What impressed them most after the visit:

The municipal construction of Qingdao City has made rapid progress in recent years, achieving astonishing results. Mayor Shen and the heads of various bureaus have shown determination, and all civil servants are full of vitality, diligently performing their duties and taking responsibility for their tasks. All municipal and rural construction projects, including education, highways, sanitation, public housing, beggar reformatories, and drug rehabilitation centers, have been planned and implemented appropriately. This is unparalleled by any other city in China and rare even in Europe and the United States. The visitors were deeply impressed and felt that the affairs of China are not difficult to manage and that the Chinese people are capable if they are willing to work diligently for the public good. Qingdao City can serve as a practical example.

Mr. Zhang Tongxuan's establishment of the Sizhong Middle School in Boye County, Hebei Province, and his training of the local population in three nearby counties demonstrate an indestructible spirit and achievement. Mr. Zhang, a former army commander and commander-in-chief, is now a member of the Hebei Provincial Government and is able to endure hardship, lead by example, and live with the youth and the people, training them personally using a combination of education and hygiene methods. This has reversed the demoralized atmosphere in the general education sector. His spirit of perseverance and determination is truly admirable.

The Northwest Industrial Company in Taiyuan is a large-scale enterprise with more than 20 large factories, such as textile, paper, machine, flour, cigarette, and chemical plants. The equipment costs for each factory are mostly over a million yuan. A copper smelting plant is currently under construction. The products of all the factories are comparable to foreign goods in quality but are priced lower. The province's people are self-sufficient in their daily necessities. This spirit of hard work is truly inspiring.

B. Aspects of education in various regions that are worthy of learning:

Students in middle schools in various provinces and cities in northern China have simple lives and strong physiques. Their spirit of hard work and endurance is worthy of emulation by the youth in the south. The school buildings and facilities in Qingdao's municipal and rural primary and secondary schools are well-equipped, military training is strict, and the methods of popularizing civil education and compulsory education are worthy of Jiangsu Province's reference. The school buildings in the Pingjin Hebei area are large in scale and well-equipped, such as Nankai Middle School, Tianjin Normal School, Ping City Normal School, and Hebei Provincial High School, which are mostly unmatched by Jiangsu Province.

Compulsory education in Shanxi Province has been implemented for many years, and its coverage has reached 80%. In the remote border areas of Chahar Province, the land is barren, and the people are poor, but the administrative staff of each school are diligent and responsible. Their hard work is commendable. The prosperity of the nation depends on healthy youth, but the development of healthy youth depends on those who have the responsibility of leading and training youth first possessing national consciousness, patriotic ideas, hard work, leading by example, and living with the youth. Only then will it be effective. After our visit to education in various regions, we found that, with the exception of a very small number of schools and a very small number of teachers, the vast majority are teaching only, not only failing to live with the students but also not asking about or caring about the students' behavior and how to be a person. If those with the responsibility of education and teachers maintain this attitude, can we train youth who are capable of saving the nation and surviving? This is an extremely important issue.

The above two issues are the most important and most difficult to solve that we felt after our visit. We would like to publicly raise them for our colleagues in the education sector to discuss together. Finally, we are very grateful for the warm reception and guidance from our colleagues in the education sector in various regions during this visit.

Today's Education Ministry Education Broadcasting Program

Topic: History Lecture

Lecturer: Shen Gangbo

Time: 4:30 PM to 5:00 PM

Frequency: 660 (Central Broadcasting Station)

Children's Educational Novel: Little Men (130), Translated by Zheng Xiaocang, Original by Louisa M. Alcott

Tomorrow, Rob will be perfectly fine, but Nan has a headache and her face is covered with cold pain relief cream, lying on Mother Bhaer's sofa. She no longer feels regret now and clearly thinks that getting lost is a good game. Mrs. Jo naturally feels unhappy seeing this situation. Therefore, she speaks seriously to Nan, wanting to make her understand the difference between freedom and indulgence, and at the same time tells several stories to deepen the effectiveness of her lecture. She hasn't decided how to punish Nan, but when she gets to a certain story, she thinks of a method, and because Mrs. Jo likes strange punishments, she decides to try it.

"All children have run away," Nan defends herself, as if it's like measles and whooping cough, very natural and inevitable.

"Not all are like that, and some who run away are never found again," Mrs. Jo replies.

"Haven't you ever gotten lost?" Nan asks, her sharp eyes able to recognize some traces of the same adventurous spirit in the woman across from her, who is somber and stitching non-stop.

Mrs. Jo smiles, admitting that she has.

"Tell me about it," Nan requests, thinking that she has gained the upper hand in this conversation.

Mrs. Jo has seen this, immediately shakes her head, indicating that she still regrets it, and then says solemnly: "I had several times, this naughtiness made my poor mother suffer a lot, until finally she cured my problem."

"How?" Nan suddenly sits up, her face full of interest.

Spring and Autumn Reflections (Rong Yu)

"Watching others carry a burden, one doesn't feel the effort," this is a common habit. People criticize officials for being incompetent and scold bosses for being idiots, but only when they become officials or bosses themselves do they realize the inappropriateness of their previous criticisms.

"One's own writing is the best," hence the many literary battles in the literary world; "Another man's wife is the best," hence the many adulterous affairs in society. If we could change these around, "Another man's writing is the best," then humble gentlemen would dedicate themselves to careful study; "One's own wife is the best," then the couple would live in harmony and there would be no divorces.

It is a good thing for a young person to be mature, but if that maturity leads to constant retreat and never advancing, the difference from a "mummy" is minimal.

Once Chinese people pass the age of sixty, they think of enjoying rural life, leaving national affairs to those who come after them. This truly commits the sin of "premature aging." In the political arena of foreign countries, there are many elderly men in their seventies who are active and vigorous, truly deserving of the saying "vigorous in old age."

Radio Stations Broadcast Gramophone Records Freely Without Interference; Gramophone Records are Not Publications and Have No Exclusive Performance Rights; Directorate General of Telecommunications Informs Broadcasting Industry of Rejection 157

Foreign record companies in this city, using the excuse of copyright for their produced records, demanded that various broadcasting radio stations pay performance fees, which caused a great dispute that has not yet been resolved. According to a report from a Datong News Agency reporter, after this incident occurred, the International Telecommunications Bureau telegraphed the Ministry of Communications and requested an interpretation from the Judicial Yuan. The bureau has now received Directive No. 17731 from the Ministry of Communications, stating that regarding whether broadcasting radio stations broadcasting gramophone records involves copyright or the Publication Law, after this Ministry requested the Judicial Yuan for interpretation, the reply from the Yuan is as follows: "The Yuan received your Ministry's public letter dated July 8, roughly stating that broadcasting radio stations broadcasting gramophone records involves copyright law or the Publication Law, and requesting an interpretation. This matter has been resolved by the Unified Interpretation of Laws and Regulations Conference of this Yuan. Gramophone records are neither publications nor copyrighted works and have no exclusive right to public performance. Purchasers exercise their ownership rights and are free to use them in any way, whether for personal entertainment or public listening. Sellers, manufacturers, and publishers may not interfere." Based on this, since the Judicial Yuan's Unified Interpretation of Laws and Regulations Conference has ruled that gramophone records are neither publications nor copyrighted works and have no exclusive right to public performance, all foreign record companies demanding performance fees from the broadcasting radio stations should be rejected. The bureau, after receiving the order, has informed the broadcasting industry association of the rejection.

Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau Notice; Strictly Arresting Those Impersonating Stamp Inspectors; Must Inquire Whether They Have a Public Security Bureau Inspection Certificate 159

Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau Director Cai Jinjun issued Government Letter No. 22, stating: "During the execution of duties, the stamp inspection personnel of this bureau all hold inspection certificates issued by this bureau as proof and are accompanied by armed police officers dispatched by the respective branch bureaus. Recently, it has been reported that some individuals are claiming to be stamp inspectors of this bureau and, under the guise of selling books explaining the Stamp Tax Law, are inspecting the account books of various shops to see if stamps have been missed. When they discover errors, they extort money by threats and do whatever they please. Unaware merchants are deceived by them, which is extremely unlawful. In addition to ordering subordinates to strictly apprehend them, this notice is hereby issued for general knowledge. In the future, if anyone without an inspection certificate from this bureau or without armed police officers accompanying them inspects stamps in shops, they are impersonating inspection personnel and should be reported to the nearest police officer to be arrested and brought to justice in order to deter unlawful acts. This notice is hereby given."

A Visit to the China Pencil Factory 163

— Huang Youxiong

I. The Beginning of Domestic Pencils II. Raw Materials for Pencil Manufacturing III. Key Points of Pencil Manufacturing IV. Pencil Lead Manufacturing Process V. Pencil Shaft Manufacturing Process VI. Mechanical Equipment VII. Other Products VIII. Brief History of the China Pencil Factory

(I) The Beginning of Domestic Pencils

A small pencil, its structure is just a round piece of wood, embedded with a thin piece of lead. One always thought the manufacturing process would not be too complicated. But if you have the opportunity to visit a pencil factory (such as the China Pencil Factory at 1176 Xiexu Road, Shanghai), you will definitely be secretly amazed and say, "I didn't expect the manufacture of pencils to be so difficult," and naturally believe in the value of resources.

Pencils were invented in England in 1565 AD; and the most famous pencil factory is the A.W.Fale factory in Germany. We often see the word Bavaria branded on pencils, which is produced in Bavaria, southern Germany, because the raw materials for making pencils are quite abundant there, and wages are cheap, so there are many pencil factories, and their products can be sold to countries all over the world. As for Japan, our eastern neighbor, although it has only been manufacturing pencils for more than twenty years, it is also able to sell well to countries with backward industries because of its low labor costs and lighter costs, and the number transported to our country for sale is huge.

The pencil seems to be a trivial item, but it is actually a necessary stationery item for primary school students today, occupying an important place in educational supplies. With so many school-age children in China, the number of pencils used is impossible to estimate. But according to last year's customs trade report, the number of pencils imported into our country has reached 1.5 million gold units. As the literacy movement is rapidly advancing and universal education is striving to be implemented, the degree of need will inevitably increase accordingly. If we still have to rely on foreign supplies, the outflow of rights and interests is unbearable to imagine. Fortunately, in recent years, the pencil manufacturing industry in China has begun. The Jiulong Pencil Factory was established earlier, and the China Pencil Factory in Shanghai has risen later. Because manufacturing pencils is still a new industry in our country, I visited the China Pencil Factory nearby. I was warmly received by Mr. Wu Qingmei, the director of the factory, who carefully explained to me. Only then did I know that the process of manufacturing pencils is not as simple as people imagine, and the quality of pencil products depends entirely on whether the work is conscientious or not. Moreover, the materials used by the factory are all domestic products of our country, which is completely domestic goods, which is especially commendable. Therefore, I am happy to record what I saw during the visit and introduce it to the people of the country.

Clay washing

(II) Raw Materials for Pencil Manufacturing

When pencils first arrived in China, people named them pencils because the material of the pencil lead was like lead. Later, people misunderstood, thinking that pencils were made of lead (maybe some people still misunderstand now). The actual raw material for making pencil leads is carbonaceous graphite, also known as black lead (Graphite), which is produced in Shanxi, Shaanxi, Hebei, Hunan, Fujian, and Jiangsu provinces in our country. Natural products contain soil or other impurities. High-quality graphite, such as the earthy graphite from Tianzhen, Shanxi, has a content of 85%, and the graphite produced in Xianqing, Hunan, is also above 80%. The best is the scaly graphite near the Qinling Mountains in Shaanxi, with a content as high as 94%.

In addition to pencil lead, the raw material for pencil leads is clay (Clay). The clay must be very fine and not mixed with sand particles, so that it can be mixed with pencil lead evenly. This is produced in large quantities in the Jiangnan area of our country, so there is no need to worry about shortage, but it needs to be washed, precipitated, and filtered.

The wood used for the pencil shell is the most important raw material. High-grade products such as Pencil Cedar and Incense Cedar are mostly produced in the United States, and the northeastern provinces of our country also produce them. But ordinary evergreen trees such as pine, fir, linden, yew, poplar, juniper, and ginkgo can also be used. The China Pencil Factory often purchases various types of wood from various parts of the country and tests them in order to select the best quality for large-scale use. The ones currently used are mostly linden and pine and fir.

(III) Key Points of Pencil Manufacturing

Manufacturing pencils is very simple in principle: mix graphite and clay to form a pencil lead, and make the wood into a pencil shaft, put in the pencil lead, and the pencil is made. But in fact, to seek excellent products while also seeking rapid work, it is necessary to have considerable machine equipment and skilled manual technology. I think readers must have had experience with inferior pencils. Now let's just list a few defects and talk about them casually. For example, when you use a pencil to write, it suddenly becomes hard and unclear. That's because the pencil lead is not fine enough, the clay is not purified, or the mixing is not even and not very strong. Another example is that the pencil lead is easy to separate from the pencil shaft. That's because the pencil lead is too thin, or the wood used is not dry enough or straight enough when it is manufactured. Sometimes one half of the pencil shaft is very soft, while the other half is very hard. This is because the wood is not selected and matched properly. Other problems such as pencil lead being easily broken and the pencil shaft being difficult to sharpen are all due to improper material matching and sloppy manufacturing work. Therefore, to make high-quality pencils, one must go through a lot of trouble.

(IV) Pencil Lead Manufacturing Process

The China Pencil Factory has equipment for washing and precipitating clay raw materials. First, the clay that is transported is washed, and then it flows through several filter cylinders to gradually precipitate the sand particles. The pure clay, which is light and fine, is then filtered on a filter press to remove the water and become mud-like clay, which is then placed on a mill and finely ground for two days using electricity before it is used. Therefore, the clay itself is extremely fine. This is the work of the clay washing and grinding department.

The pencil lead used by the China Pencil Factory is purchased from a stone crushing factory, and it has already been crushed into fine powder, but it is still not fine enough. Therefore, after mixing it with clay, it must be finely ground in a mixing mill for half a day before it is taken out and steamed dry. Then it is moved to the pencil lead kneading mortar, which is also driven by electricity. After a considerable period of pounding, the pencil lead begins to have adhesion, and then it is sent to the pencil lead rolling machine. The machine rolls the block of pencil lead into pieces of flakes. The rolling must be done more than twenty times before the pencil lead is fine enough. But because the texture is still loose, it must be compacted again. At this time, the pencil lead has become a black soft block. Then it is sent to the pencil rod pressing machine, which presses out a pencil rod about the thickness of a finger, and it is cut into small sections as it is pressed. Then, in the same way, the coarse pencil rod is pressed out to form the pencil lead, which is the general thickness and length of the pencil lead that is used.

The pencil lead made in this way is soft, so after it is bundled and dried once, it is gradually heated to a high temperature of 900 degrees in the furnace to remove moisture and harden it, and then it is steamed with oil. When it cools down, the pencil lead can be used. This is the pencil lead manufacturing process. (To be continued)

Pencil rod pressing machine

Feng Mingquan's Selections from Ancient Prose

Li Shude (940) 7:30 AM to 8:30 AM

Topic: Qu Yuan's Spring Dwelling Hall Random Notes (1)

I did not practice small regular script when I was young. However, in the past, the imperial examinations in the palace halls placed great emphasis on calligraphy. In the 30th year of Daoguang, I became a Jinshi. In the Baohe Hall examination, I was ranked first. Everyone was suspicious. Later, I learned that it was because of Duke Xiangxiang. Xiangxiang obtained my paper and greatly appreciated its writing. He told Du Wenzheng that he must place me first. The officials gathered to watch. The emperor said, "The writing is good, but how could it be done so quickly? It must be a copied old text." Xiangxiang said, "No, his poetry is also consistent. Could the poetry also be old?" The discussion was settled. Therefore, I was able to enter the Hanlin Academy. Recalling the origin of my fame, I dare not forget it at every meal.

Silver Jottings 172

— Zhi Er

The "Oriental Mae West?" of "Begonia Red" has been "politely declined" by the Star Film Company. The reason for the rejection, it is said, is to rush the production of four new films, all to be completed within the year; in fact, this is only one-third of the reason. Another third is due to unfavorable public opinion, and the final third is reportedly due to issues with the compensation.

According to reports, the so-called "Oriental Female Douglas Fairbanks," Wu Lizhu, will inaugurate the Nanyang Dance Hall today. (I remember that the inaugurator of a friend's dance hall in the past was also this woman.) In addition to the grand title of "Oriental Female Douglas Fairbanks," it seems that she can also add the title of "Small Dance Hall Inauguration Star."

At the end of 1935, Yao Zi made an "interpretation" of "1935 is Tan Ying's Year" in the Film Times. Some say that in order to avoid "193X is Tan Ying's Year" becoming just a slogan, it seems that a boss should invest in a play directed by Yao Zi and starring Tan Ying. In this way, it is believed that Tan Ying's acting genius can definitely be developed, and the box office will certainly not be bad. (Zi said: It would be even better if Cheng Bugao cooperated or co-starred).

Cathay Screens "Love Ideology" 173

"I Live For Love," is Dorothy Del Rio's new work, a grand musical love film full of lighthearted sentiment. Del Rio plays a proud and arrogant singing and dancing star in the film. At first, she is deeply in love with a famous male actor, but later a street singer wins the beauty's favor with his beautiful voice, leading to a happy marriage. The dance scenes in the film are extremely lavish, and Del Rio's acting skills are also very objective. The film is scheduled to be released at Cathay today.

Thorns and Quiet Orchid 174

"Dreams Shattered, Souls Lost" Opens 175

This Year's Masterpiece of Extreme Sadness

"Dreams Shattered, Souls Lost" (Peter Ibbetson), opening today at the Grand Theatre, is an extremely tragic literary film. Paramount's executives, because previous literary films like "Little Lord Fauntleroy" and "Little Women" have achieved great success, specially adapted this immortal masterpiece by the 19th-century British literary giant George du Maurier to the screen, and specially invited Gary Cooper and Ann Harding to play the leading roles in the film. In terms of performance, it is indeed extremely sad and moving, achieving great success. The film tells the story of a pair of lovers who are separated, but their love does not diminish, and they entrust half of their lives to the memories of their dreams. This is indeed a good work that movie fans cannot miss.

Left is a scene from the film 176

"Go to the Countryside" Mr. Wang Carries the Sedan, Little Chen Sits 177

Mr. Wang's comics have long been household names, and Mr. Wang's appearance on the screen is even more popular. Mr. Wang's portraits are everywhere in the streets and alleys. Mr. Wang has become a prominent figure in the market, the only advertising material for commodities. But this time, Mr. Wang went to the countryside. He threw away his top hat, suit, gown, and mandarin jacket, put on tattered coarse cloth clothes, and became a thoroughbred country bumpkin, leading his fat wife and daughter A Yuan to farm in the countryside. Like other petty citizens, he was affected by the wave of the world economic collapse and went bankrupt. Mr. Wang is extraordinary after all. He has the courage to be a human being. In addition to working hard in rural affairs, he also helps people carry sedan chairs to earn some "extra money" to make a few floral clothes for his little A Yuan. But he was heartbroken, Mr. Wang carried the sedan for the first time and smashed his good friend Little Chen, who had become an official. In order to curry favor with his friend, he resolutely carried the sedan for Little Chen. Because Little Chen was fat, when passing over a small bridge, Mr. Wang finally had his legs shaking due to his thin body and lack of strength. The look was a bit embarrassing. In this day and age, it's a bit "that way" for a good friend to carry a sedan for another friend to sit in.
